Derived Names Imply Divine Attributes
Refutes objection and uses linguistic logic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic names 'Samī‘' and 'Baṣīr' logically imply the existence of the attributes of hearing and sight, and how this argument is supported by consensus and linguistic principles.

Core Idea
Calling Allah 'Hearing' and 'Seeing' necessarily means He has hearing and sight.

This lesson addresses a key objection: the Quran calls Allah 'Samī‘' and 'Baṣīr' but does not explicitly mention 'hearing' and 'sight' as separate attributes. The author provides a powerful response based on the linguistic rule that a derived term (like 'Samī‘') presupposes the existence of its source (hearing). This argument is reinforced by consensus and a subtle pun in the poet's wording. Let's explore how the author proves the attributes through language and agreement.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
The objection states that the claim is for attributes (hearing and sight), but revelation only says 'He is Hearing, Seeing'. The answer: people of language understand from 'Hearing' a being that has hearing.
Notice the logical move: from a derived term to the reality of the attribute.
2
Understand the linguistic principle
The author explains that using a derived term ('Samī‘') as a description necessitates the existence of the source of derivation (hearing). This is a fundamental rule of Arabic grammar and semantics.
This principle is not just theological; it's based on how language works.
3
Observe the consensus
The author mentions that all religious communities agree that Allah is speaking, hearing, and seeing. This consensus adds weight to the argument.
Consensus here refers to the agreed-upon belief across religions.
4
Appreciate the literary point
The passage ends by noting that the poet's use of 'hearing' twice is not a repetition but a complete pun (jinās tāmm), because the first refers to the attribute and the second to the evidence.
This shows the author's depth in linguistic analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بِذِي أَتَانَا السَّمْعُ) أي : بهذه الصفات الثلاثة التي هي الكلام والسمع والبصر، أتانا المسموع؛ أي: الدليل السمعي، فالسمع بمعنى المسموع؛ وهو الدليل السمعي، وليس المراد أن السمع ورد بنفس الصفات؛ لأنه خلافُ الواقع، بل المراد أنه ورد بمشتقاتها، قال تعالى: ﴿وَكَلَّمَ اللهُ مُوسَى تَكْلِيمًا﴾ [النساء: ١٦٤]؛ أي: أزال عنه الحجاب، وأسمعه الكلام القديم ثم أعاد الحجاب وليس المراد أنه تعالى يبتدئ كلاماً ثم يسكت ؛ لأنه لم يزل متكلماً دائماً وأبداً، خلافاً للمعتزلة في قولهم: بأن المعنى أنه تعالى خلق الكلام فى شجرة وأسمعه موسى ويرد كلامهم بأن الأصل في الإطلاق الحقيقة، وما رواه القضاعي، من أن الله ناجى موسى بمئة ألف وأربعين كلمة (١) ، معناه أنه فهم معاني يُعبّر عنها بهذه العدة لا لتبعيض في نفس الكلام، ورُوي أن موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يسدُّ أذنيه عند قدومه من المناجاة لئلا يسمع كلام الخلق لكونه لا يستطيع سماعه؛ لأنه صار عنده كأشد ما يكون من أصوات البهائم المنكرة، بسبب ما ذاق من اللذة التي لا يُحاط بها عند سماع كلام من ليس كمثله شيء، وقد أشرق وجهه من النور، فما رآه أحدٌ إلا عمي، فتبرقع، وبقي البرقع على وجهه إلى أن مات وأكثر ما اشتهر في المناجاة كذب لا يليق بسيدنا موسى، وقال تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ﴾ [الشورى: ١١]، وقد ورد في الحديث: «ارْبَعُوا على أنفسكم؛ فإنكم لا تدعون أصمَّ»، وفي رواية : ولا غائباً، إنما تدعون سميعاً بصيراً (٢) ، ومعنى قوله : اربعوا على أنفسكم»؛ أشفقوا على أنفسكم؛ فهو من معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿ادْعُوا رَبَّكُمْ تَضَرُّعًا وَخُفْيَةً﴾ [الأعراف : ٥٥]، وقد أجمع أهل الملل والأديان على أنه تعالى متكلم وسميع وبصير .، فإن قيل : المدعى أن له تعالى صفتين من صفات المعاني، وهما السمع والبصر، وما في الآية والحديث وانعقد عليه الإجماع أنه تعالى سميع بصير، وهو غير المدعى، أجيب بأن أهل اللغة لا يفهمون من سميع وبصير إلا ذاتاً ثبت لها السمع والبصر؛ لأنَّ إطلاق المشتق وصفاً لشيء يقتضي ثبوت مأخذ الاشتقاق له، فثبت له المدعى بالآية والحديث والإجماع مع اعتبار ما يفهمه أهل اللغة ولا يخفى أنه لا إيطاء في كلام الناظم، بل فيه الجناسُ التام؛ لأن السمع الأول بمعنى الصفة القديمة، والسمع الثاني
His statement: 'By which the hearing came to us' meaning: by these three attributes which are speech, hearing, and sight, the hearing came to us meaning the auditory evidence. So 'hearing' is in the sense of 'what is heard', i.e., the auditory evidence. The meaning is not that the attribute 'hearing' itself came in revelation, because that is contrary to fact, but rather that its derivatives came. He said: 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' [4:164], meaning: He removed the veil from him and made him hear the eternal speech, then restored the veil. It does not mean that He begins speech then becomes silent, because He has always been speaking eternally, contrary to the Mu'tazila who say that the meaning is that Allah created speech in a tree and made Moses hear it. Their statement is refuted because the default in unqualified attribution is reality. And what al-Quda'i narrated, that Allah conversed with Moses with one hundred forty thousand words (1), its meaning is that he understood meanings expressed by this number, not that the speech itself is divided. And it is narrated that Moses, peace be upon him, used to cover his ears when returning from the intimate conversation so that he would not hear the speech of creation because he could not bear it; for it had become to him like the most unpleasant sounds of animals, due to the pleasure that cannot be encompassed when hearing the speech of the One like whom there is nothing. And his face shone with light, so no one saw him but became blind, so he veiled himself, and the veil remained on his face until he died. Most of what is famous about the intimate conversation is false and unfitting for our master Moses. And He said: 'And He is the Hearing, the Seeing' [42:11], and it has come in the hadith: 'Be gentle with yourselves, for you are not calling a deaf one,' and in another narration: 'nor an absent one, you are calling a Hearing, Seeing one' (2). The meaning of 'be gentle with yourselves' is have pity on yourselves; it is similar to His statement: 'Call upon your Lord humbly and in secret' [7:55]. And the people of all religions have agreed that He is speaking, hearing, and seeing. Then if it is said: The claim is that He has two attributes of meanings, hearing and sight, but what is in the verse and hadith and consensus is that He is Hearing and Seeing, which is different from what is claimed. The answer is that the people of language do not understand from 'Hearing' and 'Seeing' except a being that has hearing and sight, because the use of a derived term as a description for something necessitates the establishment of the source of derivation for it. So the claim is established by the verse, hadith, and consensus, considering what the people of language understand. And it is not hidden that there is no repetition (īṭā') in the poet's words, but rather there is complete pun (jinās tāmm), because the first 'hearing' means the eternal attribute, and the second 'hearing'...
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a proof from revelation for the divine attributes of speech, hearing, and sight. The author explains that the poet's phrase 'بِذِي أَتَانَا السَّمْعُ' means that the auditory evidence conveys these attributes. He then discusses the verse about Moses, refuting the Mu'tazilite interpretation that God's speech is created. He also narrates traditions about Moses' experience. Then he addresses an objection: the revelation says 'Samī' and Baṣīr' not 'al-sam' and al-basar' as attributes. The answer is that the derived terms imply the attributes by linguistic principle. The passage concludes with a linguistic note about the poet's use of 'sam'' in two senses, creating a pun.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Quran's use of 'Samī‘' and 'Baṣīr' does not prove separate attributes, as it could be metaphorical.
Correction: The author shows that linguistic convention requires that such descriptions be taken literally, thus proving the attributes.

Key Takeaway

Refuting the Objection on Divine Hearing and Seeing
Refutation of an objection using linguistic derivation and a note on poetic style.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the linguistic principle of derivation (ishtiqāq) is used to defend that Allah's names Samīʿ and Baṣīr necessarily imply the attributes of hearing and seeing.

Core Idea
Derived names prove real attributes because language itself demands it.

The objection seems plausible: the evidence calls Allah 'Hearing' and 'Seeing', but does that actually prove He has hearing and seeing as attributes? The author answers by appealing to the linguistic nature of derived words, showing that when you call something 'hearing', you are implicitly affirming that it has hearing. This lesson unpacks that argument and also clarifies a subtle point about poetic repetition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection claims that the evidence (Quran, hadith, consensus) only proves that Allah is described as Samī' and Baṣīr, not that He possesses the attributes of hearing and seeing (which are the real claim).
The objector distinguishes between the derived name and the attribute itself.
2
Examine the linguistic answer
The author argues that according to the people of language, when a derived term is used as a description, it necessarily implies that the root meaning is established for the described entity. So 'Samī'' implies hearing, and 'Baṣīr' implies seeing.
This is the key principle of ishtiqāq (derivation).
3
Confirm the conclusion
Therefore, the claimed attributes are indeed established by the verse, hadith, and consensus, considering the linguistic understanding.
4
Note the poetic clarification
The commentator adds that there is no redundancy (īṭā') in the poet's line because 'sam'' is used twice with different meanings: once for the eternal attribute and once for scriptural proof. This is perfect paronomasia (jinās tāmm).
This clarifies a separate point about the poem's wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : المدعى أن له تعالى صفتين من صفات المعاني، وهما السمع والبصر، وما في الآية والحديث وانعقد عليه الإجماع أنه تعالى سميع بصير، وهو غير المدعى، أجيب بأن أهل اللغة لا يفهمون من سميع وبصير إلا ذاتاً ثبت لها السمع والبصر؛ لأنَّ إطلاق المشتق وصفاً لشيء يقتضي ثبوت مأخذ الاشتقاق له، فثبت له المدعى بالآية والحديث والإجماع مع اعتبار ما يفهمه أهل اللغة ولا يخفى أنه لا إيطاء في كلام الناظم، بل فيه الجناسُ التام؛ لأن السمع الأول بمعنى الصفة القديمة، والسمع الثاني بمعنى الدليل السمعي على أنه تقدَّم أنها ليست من مشطور الرجز بل من كامله، وحينئذ فلا إيطاء أصلاً.
If it is said: The claim is that He, exalted, has two attributes among the attributes of meanings, namely hearing and seeing, but what is in the verse and hadith and the consensus is that He, exalted, is all-Hearing (Samī') and all-Seeing (Baṣīr), which is not the claimed [attributes]. The answer is that the people of language do not understand from 'all-Hearing' and 'all-Seeing' except an entity to which hearing and seeing are established; because applying a derived term as a description of something necessitates the establishment of the root of derivation for it. So the claimed [attributes] are established for Him by the verse, the hadith, and consensus, considering what the people of language understand. And it is not hidden that there is no repetitiveness (īṭā') in the words of the poet, but rather there is perfect paronomasia (jinās tāmm), because the first 'hearing' (sam') is in the sense of the eternal attribute, and the second 'hearing' is in the sense of the scriptural proof, given that it has been stated earlier that these [verses] are not from the truncated meter (mashṭūr al-rajaz) but from its complete form. Then there is no repetitiveness at all.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector argues: the claim is that Allah has two attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī), namely hearing and seeing. But the evidence (the verse, the hadith, and consensus) only establishes that Allah is described as 'Samī‘' and 'Baṣīr', which are derived terms, not that He has the attributes themselves. Hence the evidence does not support the claim. The answer is that linguistically, when a derived term like 'Samī‘' is used as a description, it necessarily implies that the root meaning (hearing) is established for the described entity. Therefore, the evidence does prove the attributes. The commentator then notes that there is no redundancy (īṭā’) in the poet's phrasing, because 'sam‘' appears twice: once meaning the eternal attribute, and once meaning the scriptural proof. The poet's line is a case of perfect paronomasia (jinās tāmm), and no word is wasted.

Key Terms
سميع
بصير
صفات المعاني
اشتقاق
إيطاء
جناس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that derived names like 'Samīʿ' do not necessarily imply the corresponding attribute; they are just names without entailing qualities.
Correction: The passage explains that linguistically, when a derived term is used as a description, it necessarily implies the root meaning. So 'Samīʿ' does imply hearing.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the objection that calling Allah 'Samī‘' does not prove the attribute of hearing?
A) He claims the hadith explicitly mentions the attribute of hearing.
B) He argues that a derived term necessarily implies the root meaning for the entity described.
C) He says the objection is invalid because the poet used a pun.
D) He asserts that consensus alone proves the attributes.

Key Takeaway
The linguistic principle of derivation (ishtiqāq) ensures that Allah's names like Samīʿ and Baṣīr are proof of the attributes of hearing and seeing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call Allah 'Samī‘' in your prayer, do you truly believe He hears every word, even the ones you suppress? Or is it just a habit? Will you pause after saying it to feel the weight that He is listening?
?
The objection in this lesson seems intellectual, but have you ever doubted whether Allah's attributes are real because you fear a God who sees everything about you? What secret are you unwilling to bring under His sight, and what will you do about it today?
?
The poet used the same word differently without error—are you as careful with your words about Allah? Do you ever repeat His names thoughtlessly, emptying them of meaning? Commit today to learn one name thoroughly and act on it.

The Three Opinions on Allah's Attribute of Perception
The commentator enumerates three scholarly positions on divine perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly positions on whether Allah has the attribute of perception, including the concept of suspension (waqf).

Core Idea
Disagreement on divine perception leads to three positions: affirmation, denial, and suspension.

In classical Islamic theology, scholars debated whether Allah possesses the attribute of perception (idrāk). This lesson presents the three main opinions recorded in the poem and its commentary. Understanding these positions helps clarify how theologians approach disputed attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the phrase 'khulf' (disagreement) and the three positions.
2
Identify the three opinions
The passage explicitly lists affirmation (thubūt), denial (intifā'), and suspension (waqf). Write them down.
3
Understand 'waqf'
Waqf is a deliberate methodological stance of suspending judgment, not uncertainty. The commentary clarifies this.
Contrast waqf with ignorance or doubt.
4
Note the grammatical discussion
The commentator explains why wāw is preferred over fā'. This is secondary but shows attention to precision.
This reflects the careful style of scholarly commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَهَلْ لَهُ إِدْرَاكَ اَوْ لا؟ خُلْفٌ وَعِنْدَ قَوْمٍ صَحَ فِيهِ الوَقْفُ . قوله : (فَهَلْ لَهُ ... إلخ) التعبير بواو الاستئناف أوضح من التعبير بالفاء؛ لأن هذا لا يتفرع على ما قبله ويمكن جعل الفاء للاستئناف، ويصح أن تجعل فاء الفصيحة فتكون في جواب شرط مقدر والتقدير : إذا أردت تحقيق مسألة الإدراك فأقول لك : (هل له ... إلخ)، وحاصل ما ذكره الناظم أنه قيل : بثبوتها، وقيل: بانتفائها، وقيل: بالوقف، فهي أقوال ثلاثة .
So, does He have perception (idrāk) or not? There is disagreement, and with some people suspension (waqf) is established about it. His words: ('So, does He have... etc.') The expression with the conjunction wāw of continuation is clearer than with fā', because this does not branch from what precedes it, and it is possible to make the fā' for explanation, being in answer to an implied condition, the estimation being: 'If you wish to investigate the issue of perception, then I say to you: Does He have... etc.' The summary of what the poet mentioned is that it is said: (1) affirming it, (2) denying it, and (3) suspending judgment. So they are three opinions.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration. The commentator explains the poet's line that states that there is disagreement (khulf) about whether Allah has the attribute of perception (idrāk). Some affirm it, some deny it, and some suspend judgment (waqf). The commentator also discusses the grammar: the use of wāw instead of fā' is clearer because this issue does not derive from the previous topic; fā' can still be used as an explanatory device (fā' al-faṣīḥa) in response to an implied question. The core is the three positions, which are a standard way of presenting disputed theological issues.

Key Terms
إدراك
خلف
وقف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the 'waqf' (suspension) position implies uncertainty or ignorance on the part of the scholar.
Correction: In this theological context, 'waqf' is a deliberate methodological stance of suspending judgment due to insufficient evidence, not a lack of knowledge or commitment.

Checkpoint
What are the three opinions mentioned regarding the attribute of perception (idrāk) for Allah?
A) Necessary, impossible, contingent.
B) Affirmation, denial, and suspension.
C) Eternal, originated, and both.
D) Hearing, seeing, and perceiving.

Key Takeaway
The three positions on divine perception—affirmation, denial, and suspension—illustrate how theologians handle disputed attributes with methodological precision.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a theological disagreement like the one on divine perception, do you instinctively cling to one position for comfort, or are you willing to admit uncertainty? This lesson shows that suspension of judgment can be a valid, humble response. Can you think of an area in your own faith where you need to practice that humility today?
?
Allah's perception is complete and constant. He sees and hears you at every moment—even in your private thoughts. How does that reality change the way you will speak or act in the next hour? Will you carry that awareness into your next conversation?
?
The scholars who held the three positions did not arrive at them casually; they sought evidence. In your own religious learning, have you been content to rely on what others say, or do you personally engage with the sources? What is one specific question about Allah's attributes that you will investigate directly from the Quran and Sunnah this week?

The Attribute of Takwīn: Māturīdī and Ash'arī Positions
Comparing Māturīdī and Ash'arī views on takwīn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the contrasting positions of the Māturīdīs and Ash'arīs on the attribute of bringing into existence (takwīn).

Core Idea
Māturīdīs affirm takwīn as eternal; Ash'arīs see acts as temporal effects of power.

This passage delves into one of the key differences between the two schools: the nature of the creative attribute. The Māturīdīs maintain that takwīn is an eternal attribute in Allah's essence, while the Ash'arīs reinterpret the attributes of acts as temporal relations of a created power. Read on to see how each school supports its view.

Guided Path
1
Read the Māturīdī position
Start by reading how the Māturīdīs describe takwīn as an eternal attribute that takes different names based on what it brings about.
Notice that they say it is 'eternal' and 'subsisting in His essence'.
2
Understand the objection about multiplicity
Some scholars argued that if each name (e.g., ījād, iḥyā') were a distinct eternal attribute, that would multiply eternal beings. This is a criticism within the debate.
3
Examine the Ash'arī negation
Read how the Ash'arīs completely reject takwīn as an eternal attribute and instead consider the attributes of acts as temporal attachments of the effectuated power (qudra tanjīziyya).
This is a fundamental difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اختلف أيضاً في صفة التكوين، فأثبتها الماتريدية، وعليه فهي صفةٌ قديمة قائمة بذاته تعالى يُوجد بها ويُعدم بها، لكن إن تعلقت بالوجود تُسمى إيجاداً ، وإن تعلقت بالعدم تُسمى إعداماً، وإن تعلقت بالحياة تُسمى إحياء وهكذا، فصفات الأفعال عندهم صفة التكوين وهي قديمة، وذهب بعضهم إلى أن هذه قديمة ؛ لأنها هي كلها صفات متعددة، وفيه تكثير القدماء جدًّا ؛ ونفاها الأشاعرة وجعلوا صفات الأفعال تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة. فإن قيل على طريقة الماتريدية ما وظيفة القدرة عندهم؟ أجيب بأن وظيفتها تهيئة الممكن بحيث تجعله قابلاً للوجود والعدم، ورد بأن قبوله لذلك ذاتي له، وأجيب بأن الذاتي إنما هو القبول الإمكاني، بخلاف القبول الاستعدادي القريب من الفعل.
And there is also disagreement about the attribute of bringing into existence (takwīn). The Māturīdīs affirm it, and according to them it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, exalted, by which He brings into existence and brings into non-existence. But if it is related to existence, it is called bringing into existence (ījād); if related to non-existence, it is called bringing into non-existence (i‘dām); if related to life, it is called giving life (iḥyā'), and so on. Thus, the attributes of acts (ṣifāt al-af‘āl) according to them are the attribute of takwīn, and it is eternal. Some went to the view that these [names] are eternal because they are all multiple attributes, and in that there is a great multiplication of eternal beings. The Ash‘arīs negated it and made the attributes of acts temporal attachments of the effectuated power (qudra tanjīziyya). If it is said: according to the Māturīdī method, what is the function of power (qudra)? It is answered: its function is to prepare the possible [entity] such that it makes it receptive to existence and non-existence. It is objected that its receptivity to that is essential (dhātī) to it. And it is answered that the essential is only the possibilistic receptivity (qabūl imkānī), unlike the dispositional receptivity (qabūl isti‘dādī) close to the act.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a comparative and disputational passage. It first states that there is disagreement about the attribute of takwīn (bringing into existence). The Māturīdīs affirm it as an eternal attribute subsisting in Allah's essence, by which He brings things into existence and non-existence. However, the names of the specific acts (e.g., ījād, i‘dām, iḥyā') are just relations of that single eternal attribute to different objects. Thus, all so-called 'attributes of acts' reduce to one eternal attribute, takwīn. Some theologians argued that each specific name (e.g., creating, providing) is a separate eternal attribute, leading to a multiplication of eternal entities, which is problematic. The Ash‘arīs, on the other hand, negate takwīn as an eternal attribute altogether, and instead consider the attributes of acts as temporal 'affections' (ta‘alluqāt) of the power (qudra) that is created at the moment of the act (qudra tanjīziyya ḥāditha). Then an objection is raised: in the Māturīdī system, what is the role of power (qudra) if takwīn does the creating? The answer is that power prepares the possible entity, making it receptive to existence or non-existence. An objection counters that the possible entity's receptivity is essential (dhātī) to it, so power is superfluous. The final answer distinguishes between essential possibilistic receptivity (qabūl imkānī) and dispositional receptivity (qabūl isti‘dādī) that is close to the act; the power effects the latter. The passage thus presents a complex intra-school debate.

Key Terms

ماتريدية
أشاعرة
صفات الأفعال
قدرة تنجيزية

The Role of Power in the Māturīdī System: Objection and Answer
Objection and answer about the function of power in Māturīdī theology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Māturīdīs defend the role of power (qudra) alongside the eternal attribute of takwīn.

Core Idea
Power prepares the possible entity with a dispositional receptivity, not essential.

After presenting the Māturīdī position on takwīn, the text anticipates a crucial objection: if takwīn creates, what is the function of power (qudra)? The answer unfolds a subtle distinction between two kinds of receptivity in the possible entity. This lesson unpacks that objection-and-answer sequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the first answer
The objection asks: What is the role of power in the Māturīdī system? The answer says it prepares the possible entity to be receptive.
Notice the terminology: 'تهيئة الممكن'.
2
Understand the counter-objection
The response is met with a counter: the possible entity already has essential receptivity (qabūl imkānī), so preparation is unnecessary.
3
Study the final distinction
The final answer distinguishes between essential possibilistic receptivity and dispositional receptivity (qabūl isti‘dādī) that is close to the act. Power effects the latter.
This is the key point: power is not redundant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اختلف أيضاً في صفة التكوين، فأثبتها الماتريدية، وعليه فهي صفةٌ قديمة قائمة بذاته تعالى يُوجد بها ويُعدم بها، لكن إن تعلقت بالوجود تُسمى إيجاداً ، وإن تعلقت بالعدم تُسمى إعداماً، وإن تعلقت بالحياة تُسمى إحياء وهكذا، فصفات الأفعال عندهم صفة التكوين وهي قديمة، وذهب بعضهم إلى أن هذه قديمة ؛ لأنها هي كلها صفات متعددة، وفيه تكثير القدماء جدًّا ؛ ونفاها الأشاعرة وجعلوا صفات الأفعال تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة. فإن قيل على طريقة الماتريدية ما وظيفة القدرة عندهم؟ أجيب بأن وظيفتها تهيئة الممكن بحيث تجعله قابلاً للوجود والعدم، ورد بأن قبوله لذلك ذاتي له، وأجيب بأن الذاتي إنما هو القبول الإمكاني، بخلاف القبول الاستعدادي القريب من الفعل.
And there is also disagreement about the attribute of bringing into existence (takwīn). The Māturīdīs affirm it, and according to them it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, exalted, by which He brings into existence and brings into non-existence. But if it is related to existence, it is called bringing into existence (ījād); if related to non-existence, it is called bringing into non-existence (i‘dām); if related to life, it is called giving life (iḥyā'), and so on. Thus, the attributes of acts (ṣifāt al-af‘āl) according to them are the attribute of takwīn, and it is eternal. Some went to the view that these [names] are eternal because they are all multiple attributes, and in that there is a great multiplication of eternal beings. The Ash‘arīs negated it and made the attributes of acts temporal attachments of the effectuated power (qudra tanjīziyya). If it is said: according to the Māturīdī method, what is the function of power (qudra)? It is answered: its function is to prepare the possible [entity] such that it makes it receptive to existence and non-existence. It is objected that its receptivity to that is essential (dhātī) to it. And it is answered that the essential is only the possibilistic receptivity (qabūl imkānī), unlike the dispositional receptivity (qabūl isti‘dādī) close to the act.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a comparative and disputational passage. It first states that there is disagreement about the attribute of takwīn (bringing into existence). The Māturīdīs affirm it as an eternal attribute subsisting in Allah's essence, by which He brings things into existence and non-existence. However, the names of the specific acts (e.g., ījād, i‘dām, iḥyā') are just relations of that single eternal attribute to different objects. Thus, all so-called 'attributes of acts' reduce to one eternal attribute, takwīn. Some theologians argued that each specific name (e.g., creating, providing) is a separate eternal attribute, leading to a multiplication of eternal entities, which is problematic. The Ash‘arīs, on the other hand, negate takwīn as an eternal attribute altogether, and instead consider the attributes of acts as temporal 'affections' (ta‘alluqāt) of the power (qudra) that is created at the moment of the act (qudra tanjīziyya ḥāditha). Then an objection is raised: in the Māturīdī system, what is the role of power (qudra) if takwīn does the creating? The answer is that power prepares the possible entity, making it receptive to existence or non-existence. An objection counters that the possible entity's receptivity is essential (dhātī) to it, so power is superfluous. The final answer distinguishes between essential possibilistic receptivity (qabūl imkānī) and dispositional receptivity (qabūl isti‘dādī) that is close to the act; the power effects the latter. The passage thus presents a complex intra-school debate.

?
If power only provides readiness, then the actual existence of anything is a direct gift from God. What in your life are you taking credit for, forgetting that God not only made it possible but actually brought it into being?

The Maturidi-Ash'ari Dispute Over Takwin
The commentator presents the dispute over takwin and a dialectical exchange.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi-A sh'ari dispute over the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) and the arguments concerning the function of divine power.

Core Idea
Takwin is an eternal attribute for Maturidis but a temporal relation for Ash'aris.

This passage introduces a key intra-Sunni debate over whether God's act of creation is an eternal attribute or a temporal relation of power. You will encounter the Maturidi view of takwin as a single eternal attribute that takes different names, and the Ash'ari rejection of that view, along with a dialectical exchange about the function of power.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the first part of the passage where the Maturidi and Ash'ari views are contrasted. Note what each school affirms or denies about takwin.
The Maturidis affirm takwin as an eternal attribute; the Ash'aris deny it and consider attributes of actions as temporal relations.
2
Understand the dialectic
Follow the question-and-answer sequence: what is the function of power according to the Maturidis? Then note the objection and response about receptivity.
The distinction between essential receptivity and receptivity of preparedness is crucial.
3
Reflect on the underlying issue
Consider why this dispute matters for understanding God's attributes and actions. Both schools agree God creates, but differ on whether the attribute of creation is eternal or not.
This debate touches on the problem of divine simplicity and the multiplicity of eternal entities.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اختلف أيضاً في صفة التكوين، فأثبتها الماتريدية، وعليه فهي صفةٌ قديمة قائمة بذاته تعالى يُوجد بها ويُعدم بها، لكن إن تعلقت بالوجود تُسمى إيجاداً، وإن تعلقت بالعدم تُسمى إعداماً، وإن تعلقت بالحياة تُسمى إحياء وهكذا، فصفات الأفعال عندهم صفة التكوين وهي قديمة، وذهب بعضهم إلى أن هذه قديمة؛ لأنها هي كلها صفات متعددة، وفيه تكثير القدماء جدًّا؛ ونفاها الأشاعرة وجعلوا صفات الأفعال تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة. فإن قيل على طريقة الماتريدية ما وظيفة القدرة عندهم؟ أجيب بأن وظيفتها تهيئة الممكن بحيث تجعله قابلاً للوجود والعدم، ورد بأن قبوله لذلك ذاتي له، وأجيب بأن الذاتي إنما هو القبول الإمكاني، بخلاف القبول الاستعدادي القريب من الفعل.
And there is also disagreement concerning the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The Maturidis affirm it, and accordingly it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, by which He brings into existence and annihilates. But if it is related to existence it is called 'bringing into existence' (ijad), and if related to non-existence it is called 'annihilating' (i'dam), and if related to life it is called 'giving life' (ihya), and so on. Thus the attributes of actions according to them are the attribute of takwin, and it is eternal. Some others went that these [individual attributes] are eternal because they are all multiple attributes, but this involves excessive multiplicity of eternal entities. The Ash'aris denied it and made the attributes of actions to be relations of the contingent power (qudra) that occurs. If it is said according to the Maturidi way: what is the function of power according to them? It is answered: its function is to prepare the possible so as to make it receptive to existence and non-existence. It is objected that its receptivity to that is essential (dhati) to it. It is answered: the essential receptivity is only the receptivity of possibility (imkani), contrary to the receptivity of preparedness (isti'dadi) that is close to the act.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents the dispute over the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The commentator first states that there is disagreement. He then explains the Maturidi position: takwin is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, by which He creates and annihilates. It is a single attribute that takes different names depending on its relation: ijad (bringing into existence), i'dam (annihilating), ihya (giving life), etc. Thus, for the Maturidis, the attributes of actions are reduced to this one eternal attribute. Some others (unspecified) argued that each of these is a separate eternal attribute, but the commentator notes that this would multiply eternal entities excessively. The Ash'aris, on the other hand, deny takwin and consider attributes of actions to be temporal relations (ta'alliqat) of the contingent power. The passage then presents a question-and-answer: if the Maturidis affirm takwin, what role does power (qudra) play? The answer: power prepares the possible to receive existence or non-existence. This is objected to by saying that the possible's receptivity is intrinsic (dhati). The reply distinguishes between essential receptivity (al-qabul al-imkani, the receptivity of possibility) and receptivity of preparedness (al-qabul al-isti'dadi), which is closer to the actual act. This argument is typical in kalam.

Definition of Idrak and Its Types
Definition of idrak and its threefold classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of idrak for contingent beings and for God, and the classification of idrak into three types according to kalam.

Core Idea
Idrak is the perception of realities, and for God it is an eternal attribute with three types.

This lesson begins by defining what perception means for created beings—a mental grasp of the perceived reality—and then explains how this attribute applies to God in a transcendent manner. The commentator also notes the scholarly debate on whether it is one attribute or three, settling on the threefold division found in kalam books.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition for contingent beings
Read how idrak is defined as the conceptualization of the perceived thing by the perceiver. Note the grammatical distinction between mudrik (perceiver) and mudrak (perceived).
This is a technical philosophical definition.
2
Grasp the divine attribute of idrak
Learn that for God, idrak is an eternal attribute by which He perceives tangibles, odors, and tastes without contact or qualification. The reason given is that contact is merely customary.
3
Identify the three types of idrak
See that kalam books list three attributes: perception of tangibles, perception of odors, and perception of tastes, though some later scholars consider it one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (إِدْرَاكُ) هو في حق الحادث تصور حقيقة الشيء المدرَك عند المدرك؛ أي : تصور حقيقة الشيء المدرك - بفتح الراء على صيغة اسم المفعول ـ عند المدرك - بكسرها على صورة اسم الفاعل. وأما في حقه تعالى على القول به فهو صفة قديمةٌ قائمة بذاته تعالى تسمى الإدراك، يدرك بها الملموسات كالنعومة والخشونة والمشمومات كالرائحة الطيبة والمذوقات كالحلاوة من غير اتصال بمحالها التي هي الأجسام، ولا تكيف بكيفياتها؛ لأن ذلك إنما هو عادي وقد ينفك، وقيل : يدرك بها كل موجود. والذي صرّح به بعض المتأخرين أنها صفةٌ واحدةٌ، لكن الواقع في كتب الكلام أنها ثلاث صفات : إدراك الملموسات، وإدراك المشمومات وإدراك المذوقات، واستدل القائلون بإثباتها - وهم القاضي الباقلاني وإمام الحرمين ومن وافقهما - بأنها كمال وكل كمال واجب الله؛ لأنه لو لم يتصف بها لاتصف بضدها وهو نقص، والنقص عليه تعالى محال، فوجب أن يتصف بها على ما يليق به من غير اتصال بالأجسام، ومن غير وصول اللذات والآلام له تعالى . فلا يتصور الاتصال وقوله أَوْ لا؛ أي أو ليس له إدراك أي صفة تسمى الإدراك كما ذهب إليه جمع واستدلوا على ذلك بأنه لو اتصف تعالى بها لزم الاتصال بمحالها تلازماً عقليا، انفكاكه واللازم مستحيل في حقه تعالى واستحالة اللازم وهو توجب استحالة الملزوم وهو اتصافه تعالى بها، لكن الأولون لا يُسلّمون أن بين الاتصاف بها والاتصال بمحالها تلازماً عقليًّا؛ لما تقدم من أنه يجعله عاديا ويقبل الانفكاك، ودعوى أنه تعالى لو لم يتصف بها لاتصف بضدها فاسدة، لمنافاة العلم
His statement: (إِدْرَاكُ) - perception - in the case of the contingent is the conceptualization of the reality of the perceived thing by the perceiver; i.e., the conceptualization of the reality of the thing perceived (with fatha on the ra as the passive participle) in the perceiver (with kasra on the ra as the active participle). As for His right - exalted be He - according to the one who affirms it, it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence called perception, by which He perceives tangible things such as softness and roughness, and odors such as pleasant fragrance, and tastes such as sweetness, without contact with their loci which are bodies, and without being qualified by their qualities; because that is merely customary and can be absent. And it is said that by it He perceives every existent. Some later scholars explicitly stated that it is a single attribute, but what is found in the books of kalam is that it is three attributes: perception of tangible things, perception of odors, and perception of tastes. And those who affirm it - and they are al-Qadi al-Baqillani, Imam al-Haramayn, and those who agreed with them - argued that it is a perfection, and every perfection is obligatory for God; because if He were not described with it, He would be described with its opposite which is deficiency, and deficiency is impossible for Him - exalted be He. So it is necessary that He be described with it in a manner befitting Him, without contact with bodies, and without the experience of pleasures and pains for Him - exalted be He. Thus contact is inconceivable. And his statement 'or not' means: or does He not have perception i.e., an attribute called perception, as some held, and they argued that if He were described with it, contact with their loci would necessarily follow as a rational entailment, and such contact is impossible for Him - exalted be He, and the impossibility of the consequent necessitates the impossibility of the antecedent, which is His being described with it. But the former (the affirmers) do not concede that there is a rational entailment between being described with it and contact with their loci; because it has been stated previously that he makes it customary and it can be absent. And the claim that if He were not described with it He would be described with its opposite is false, because it contradicts [knowledge].
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a definition and argumentation regarding the attribute of perception (idrak). It begins by defining idrak for contingent beings: it is the conceptualization of the perceived thing by the perceiver. For God, if affirmed, idrak is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence by which He perceives tangibles, odors, tastes, etc., without contact or qualification, because such contact is merely customary and not necessary. Some say it is a single attribute, but kalam books mention three types. Then the passage presents the proof of those who affirm idrak for God: al-Baqillani and Imam al-Haramayn. Their argument: idrak is a perfection, and every perfection is obligatory for God; the opposite (lack of perception) would be a deficiency, and deficiency is impossible for God. Therefore, God must have perception in a way befitting Him, without contact or sensation. Then the passage presents the objection of those who deny idrak: they argue that if God had perception, it would necessarily entail contact with the loci of perception (bodies), which is impossible for God; thus, the impossibility of the consequent implies the impossibility of the antecedent, so God does not have perception. The affirmers respond by denying the rational entailment: the connection is merely customary, not necessary, as previously mentioned. They also refute the claim that lack of perception would imply its opposite (a deficiency), arguing that this is false because it contradicts [the knowledge that God is perfect without it]. The passage is cut off, but the main elements are clear.

Key Terms
إدراك (idrak)
تصور (tasawwur)
مدرك (mudrik/mudrak)
عادي (adi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's perception is similar to human perception involving physical contact with objects.
Correction: God's perception is without contact or qualification; contact is merely customary and not necessary.

Checkpoint

A) Because contact is impossible for God
B) Because contact is merely customary and can be absent
C) Because God is not affected by pleasure or pain
D) Because perception does not require contact

Key Takeaway
Idrak for God is an eternal attribute that perceives qualities without contact, and is divided into three types according to kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
God perceives your every hidden action, feeling, and thought without any need for contact or physical proximity. If you truly believed that, would you still commit that secret sin you rationalize? What will you do today to act as if you are always in His presence?
?
The passage says God's perception is eternal and unchanging, while your own senses are fleeting and limited. How does this contrast confront your tendency to forget that He sees even your private struggles? What specific reminder will you place in your daily routine to keep this awareness alive?
?
God's perception of tangibles, odors, and tastes is without contact or being affected by qualities. This means He knows the full reality of everything you encounter. How does this change the way you approach a moment of sin that you thought was hidden? Will you ask His forgiveness now, or wait until it is too late?

Arguments for and against God's Perception
Proof for and against God's perception, with rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational arguments used to affirm and deny the attribute of perception for God, including the rebuttal to the denial argument.

Core Idea
Affirmers argue perception is a perfection; deniers say it entails contact; affirmers deny the entailment.

This lesson presents the core theological debate: those who affirm perception argue it is a perfection obligatory for God, while those who deny it argue it leads to impossible consequences. The commentator explains both positions and the counterargument, showing how the affirmers reject the claim of a rational entailment between perception and contact.

Guided Path
1
Study the proof of the affirmers
Read the argument that idrak is a perfection, and God must possess all perfections, so He must have perception without contact or sensation.
This is a classic kalam argument based on the impossibility of deficiency.
2
Understand the objection of the deniers
Learn the counterargument: if God had perception, it would necessarily entail contact with physical loci, which is impossible for God; therefore, He does not have perception.
This uses the principle of talazum (entailment).
3
Examine the rebuttal
The affirmers respond that the entailment is not rational (aqli) but merely customary (adi), so it can be denied. They also refute the claim that lack of perception would be a deficiency.
This hinges on the distinction between rational and customary connections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (إِدْرَاكُ) هو في حق الحادث تصور حقيقة الشيء المدرَك عند المدرك؛ أي : تصور حقيقة الشيء المدرك - بفتح الراء على صيغة اسم المفعول ـ عند المدرك - بكسرها على صورة اسم الفاعل. وأما في حقه تعالى على القول به فهو صفة قديمةٌ قائمة بذاته تعالى تسمى الإدراك، يدرك بها الملموسات كالنعومة والخشونة والمشمومات كالرائحة الطيبة والمذوقات كالحلاوة من غير اتصال بمحالها التي هي الأجسام، ولا تكيف بكيفياتها؛ لأن ذلك إنما هو عادي وقد ينفك، وقيل : يدرك بها كل موجود. والذي صرّح به بعض المتأخرين أنها صفةٌ واحدةٌ، لكن الواقع في كتب الكلام أنها ثلاث صفات : إدراك الملموسات، وإدراك المشمومات وإدراك المذوقات، واستدل القائلون بإثباتها - وهم القاضي الباقلاني وإمام الحرمين ومن وافقهما - بأنها كمال وكل كمال واجب الله؛ لأنه لو لم يتصف بها لاتصف بضدها وهو نقص، والنقص عليه تعالى محال، فوجب أن يتصف بها على ما يليق به من غير اتصال بالأجسام، ومن غير وصول اللذات والآلام له تعالى . فلا يتصور الاتصال وقوله أَوْ لا؛ أي أو ليس له إدراك أي صفة تسمى الإدراك كما ذهب إليه جمع واستدلوا على ذلك بأنه لو اتصف تعالى بها لزم الاتصال بمحالها تلازماً عقليا، انفكاكه واللازم مستحيل في حقه تعالى واستحالة اللازم وهو توجب استحالة الملزوم وهو اتصافه تعالى بها، لكن الأولون لا يُسلّمون أن بين الاتصاف بها والاتصال بمحالها تلازماً عقليًّا؛ لما تقدم من أنه يجعله عاديا ويقبل الانفكاك، ودعوى أنه تعالى لو لم يتصف بها لاتصف بضدها فاسدة، لمنافاة العلم
His statement: (إِدْرَاكُ) - perception - in the case of the contingent is the conceptualization of the reality of the perceived thing by the perceiver; i.e., the conceptualization of the reality of the thing perceived (with fatha on the ra as the passive participle) in the perceiver (with kasra on the ra as the active participle). As for His right - exalted be He - according to the one who affirms it, it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence called perception, by which He perceives tangible things such as softness and roughness, and odors such as pleasant fragrance, and tastes such as sweetness, without contact with their loci which are bodies, and without being qualified by their qualities; because that is merely customary and can be absent. And it is said that by it He perceives every existent. Some later scholars explicitly stated that it is a single attribute, but what is found in the books of kalam is that it is three attributes: perception of tangible things, perception of odors, and perception of tastes. And those who affirm it - and they are al-Qadi al-Baqillani, Imam al-Haramayn, and those who agreed with them - argued that it is a perfection, and every perfection is obligatory for God; because if He were not described with it, He would be described with its opposite which is deficiency, and deficiency is impossible for Him - exalted be He. So it is necessary that He be described with it in a manner befitting Him, without contact with bodies, and without the experience of pleasures and pains for Him - exalted be He. Thus contact is inconceivable. And his statement 'or not' means: or does He not have perception i.e., an attribute called perception, as some held, and they argued that if He were described with it, contact with their loci would necessarily follow as a rational entailment, and such contact is impossible for Him - exalted be He, and the impossibility of the consequent necessitates the impossibility of the antecedent, which is His being described with it. But the former (the affirmers) do not concede that there is a rational entailment between being described with it and contact with their loci; because it has been stated previously that he makes it customary and it can be absent. And the claim that if He were not described with it He would be described with its opposite is false, because it contradicts [knowledge].
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a definition and argumentation regarding the attribute of perception (idrak). It begins by defining idrak for contingent beings: it is the conceptualization of the perceived thing by the perceiver. For God, if affirmed, idrak is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence by which He perceives tangibles, odors, tastes, etc., without contact or qualification, because such contact is merely customary and not necessary. Some say it is a single attribute, but kalam books mention three types. Then the passage presents the proof of those who affirm idrak for God: al-Baqillani and Imam al-Haramayn. Their argument: idrak is a perfection, and every perfection is obligatory for God; the opposite (lack of perception) would be a deficiency, and deficiency is impossible for God. Therefore, God must have perception in a way befitting Him, without contact or sensation. Then the passage presents the objection of those who deny idrak: they argue that if God had perception, it would necessarily entail contact with the loci of perception (bodies), which is impossible for God; thus, the impossibility of the consequent implies the impossibility of the antecedent, so God does not have perception. The affirmers respond by denying the rational entailment: the connection is merely customary, not necessary, as previously mentioned. They also refute the claim that lack of perception would imply its opposite (a deficiency), arguing that this is false because it contradicts [the knowledge that God is perfect without it]. The passage is cut off, but the main elements are clear.

نقص (naqs)
اتصال (ittisal)
محال (mahall)
تلازم (talazum)
عقلي (aqli)
عادي (adi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The deniers' argument is logically unassailable and the affirmers have no response.
Correction: Affirmers reject the claim of rational entailment, asserting the connection is merely customary.

Checkpoint
How do the affirmers of idrak respond to the deniers' argument that perception entails contact?
A) They accept the entailment but argue contact is not impossible
B) They deny the entailment is rational, saying it is only customary
C) They argue that God can have contact in a spiritual way
D) They reject the perfection argument

Key Takeaway
The debate over God's perception hinges on whether the connection between perception and contact is rational or customary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God perceives every thought, feeling, and action of yours, does that make you want to run to Him or hide? What specific habit will you change this week because of this awareness?
?
If you truly believed that God's perception of you is a perfection that brings Him no deficiency, would you still fear His knowledge of your worst moments? What would it take for you to fully trust that He sees you and still accepts you?
?
The deniers worried that perception implies contact with imperfection. Have you ever avoided drawing close to God because you felt too dirty? How does the lesson's emphasis on 'in a manner befitting Him' free you to come as you are?

Definition and Proof of the Attribute of Perception (Idrak)
Definition and proof of idrak with objections and suspension.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the attribute of perception (idrak) for Allah, the rational proof for its affirmation, the objection based on entailment of physical connection, and the position of suspension of judgment.

Core Idea
Perfection demands perception, but does it require physical contact?

This lesson examines the attribute of idrak (perception) as a divine attribute. The author first defines it for contingent beings and then for Allah. He presents the proof from perfection (kamaal) used by al-Baqillani and al-Juwayni, the objection from rational entailment of connection, and the reply distinguishing customary from rational. Finally, it discusses the disagreement based on prior proofs and the recommendation of suspension.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of idrak
Read the definition of idrak for contingent beings and for Allah, noting the contrast.
The definition for Allah emphasizes no physical connection.
2
Understand the proof of affirmation
Understand the argument that idrak is a perfection; lacking it would imply deficiency, which is impossible for Allah.
3
Analyze the objection and response
Analyze the objection that idrak would entail physical connection, and the response that the entailment is merely customary, not rational.
4
Explore the three positions
Explore the three positions on idrak: affirmation, denial, and suspension, noting their bases.
Suspension is considered safer due to conflicting evidences.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (إِدْرَاكُ) هو في حق الحادث تصور حقيقة الشيء المدرَك عند المدرك؛ أي : تصور حقيقة الشيء المدرك - بفتح الراء على صيغة اسم المفعول ـ عند المدرك - بكسرها على صورة اسم الفاعل. وأما في حقه تعالى على القول به فهو صفة قديمةٌ قائمة بذاته تعالى تسمى الإدراك، يدرك بها الملموسات كالنعومة والخشونة والمشمومات كالرائحة الطيبة والمذوقات كالحلاوة من غير اتصال بمحالها التي هي الأجسام، ولا تكيف بكيفياتها ؛ لأن ذلك إنما هو عادي وقد ينفك ، وقيل : يدرك بها كل موجود. والذي صرّح به بعض المتأخرين أنها صفةٌ واحدةٌ، لكن الواقع في كتب الكلام أنها ثلاث صفات : إدراك الملموسات، وإدراك المشمومات وإدراك المذوقات، واستدل القائلون بإثباتها - وهم القاضي الباقلاني وإمام الحرمين ومن وافقهما - بأنها كمال وكل كمال واجب الله ؛ لأنه لو لم يتصف بها لاتصف بضدها وهو نقص، والنقص عليه تعالى محال، فوجب أن يتصف بها على ما يليق به من غير اتصال بالأجسام، ومن غير وصول اللذات والآلام له تعالى . فلا يتصور الاتصال . وقوله أَوْ لا ؛ أي أو ليس له إدراك أي صفة تسمى الإدراك كما ذهب إليه جمع واستدلوا على ذلك بأنه لو اتصف تعالى بها لزم الاتصال بمحالها تلازماً عقليا ، انفكاكه واللازم مستحيل في حقه تعالى واستحالة اللازم وهو توجب استحالة الملزوم وهو اتصافه تعالى بها، لكن الأولون لا يُسلّمون(۳) أن بين الاتصاف بها والاتصال بمحالها تلازماً عقليًّا؛ لما تقدم من أنه يجعله عاديا ويقبل الانفكاك، ودعوى أنه تعالى لو لم يتصف بها لاتصف بضدها فاسدة، لمنافاة العلم الإلهيات الواجب له تعالى لذلك الضد ؛ لأنَّ علمه تعالى محيط بمتعلقاتها ؛ فهو كافٍ عنها حيث لم يرد سمع، ولا دلّ عليها فعله تعالى كخلق العالم؛ لأنه لا يتوقف عليها . وقوله : (خُلْفُ ) أي : في جواب ذلك اختلاف؛ فهو مبتدأ خبره محذوف(۱)، وهذا الاختلاف مبني على الاختلاف في دليل الصفات الثلاثة السابقة التي هي الكلام والسمع والبصر، فمن أثبتها بالدليل العقلي وهو أنها صفاتُ كمال فلو لم يتصف بها لا تصف بأضدادها وهي نقائص والنقص عليه تعالى محال، أثبت هذه الصفة التي هي صفة الإدراك، ومن أثبتها بالدليل السمعي المتقدم نفى الصفة المذكورة؛ لأنه لم يرد بها سمع . قوله : (وَعِنْدَ قَوْم صَحَ فِيهِ الوَقْفُ) أي : وصح التوقف عن القول بإثبات الإدراك : ونفيه عند قوم من المتكلمين كالمقترح وابن التلمساني وبعض المتأخرين، لتعارض الأدلة، فهؤلاء القوم لا يجزمون بثبوت الإدراك كأهل القول الأول، ولا يجزمون بنفيه كأهل القول الثاني وهذا القول أسلم وأصح من القولين الأولين، وكما اختلف في الإدراك اختلف في الكون مدركاً، والأصح الوقف عن ذلك.
His saying: (Perception) – regarding the contingent it is the conception of the reality of the perceived thing with the perceiver; i.e., conception of the reality of the perceived thing (with fath on the ra of the passive participle) with the perceiver (with kasr on the form of the active participle). As for regarding Him, Exalted, according to the opinion of affirming it, it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, Exalted, called perception, by which tangible things like softness and roughness, and smelled things like pleasant scent, and tasted things like sweetness are perceived, without connection to their loci which are bodies, and without being qualified by their qualities; because that is merely customary and may be separated. And it is said: by it every existent is perceived. And what some later scholars stated is that it is a single attribute, but what occurs in the books of kalam is that they are three attributes: perception of tangible things, perception of smelled things, and perception of tasted things. And those who affirm it – and they are al-Qadi al-Baqillani and Imam al-Haramayn and those who agreed with them – argued that it is perfection, and every perfection is necessary for Allah; because if He were not qualified with it He would be qualified with its opposite which is deficiency, and deficiency upon Him, Exalted, is impossible, so it is necessary that He be qualified with it in a manner befitting Him, without connection to bodies, and without reaching of pleasures and pains to Him, Exalted. So there is no conception of connection. And His saying: 'or not' – i.e., or He has no perception, i.e., an attribute called perception, as a group went, and they argued that if He, Exalted, were qualified with it, connection to its loci would necessarily follow, by a rational entailment, and its separation [is impossible]; the consequent is impossible in His, Exalted, right, and the impossibility of the consequent necessitates the impossibility of the antecedent, which is His being qualified with it. But the first group do not concede that there is a rational entailment between being qualified with it and connection to its loci, due to what preceded, that he considers it customary and possible to separate. And the claim that if He, Exalted, were not qualified with it He would be qualified with its opposite is invalid, because it would contradict knowledge – the divine matters – that is necessary for Him, Exalted, for that opposite; because His knowledge, Exalted, encompasses its objects; so it suffices for them where no transmitted evidence came, nor does His action, Exalted, like creating the world indicate it; because it does not depend on them. And His saying: (disagreement) – i.e., in answer to that there is disagreement; it is a subject whose predicate is deleted, and this disagreement is based on the disagreement concerning the proof of the three previous attributes, which are speech, hearing, and sight. Whoever affirmed them through rational proof – namely that they are attributes of perfection, and if He were not qualified with them He would be qualified with their opposites which are deficiencies, and deficiency upon Him, Exalted, is impossible – affirmed this attribute, which is the attribute of perception. And whoever affirmed them through the aforementioned transmitted proof denied the mentioned attribute, because no transmitted evidence came for it. His saying: (and with a group the suspension of judgment therein is valid) – i.e., suspension of judgment concerning affirming or denying perception is valid with a group of speculative theologians, like al-Muqrih, Ibn al-Tilmisani, and some later scholars, due to the conflicting evidences. So these groups do not decisively affirm perception like the people of the first opinion, nor do they decisively deny it like the people of the second opinion. And this opinion is safer and more correct than the first two opinions. And just as disagreement occurred regarding perception, disagreement occurred regarding being a perceiver, and the most correct is suspension of judgment concerning that.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a definition and argumentative discussion of the attribute of perception (idrak). The author first defines idrak in relation to contingent beings as the conception of the reality of the perceived thing with the perceiver. Then for Allah, according to those who affirm it, it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, by which He perceives tangible, smelled, and tasted things without physical contact or being qualified by their qualities, because contact is merely customary and can be separated. Some say it is one attribute, but kalam books treat it as three. The author then presents the proof of those who affirm it (al-Baqillani and al-Juwayni): it is perfection, and all perfection is necessary for Allah, otherwise He would be qualified with deficiency. The objectors argue that if Allah had perception, it would entail physical contact, which is impossible. The first group responds that entailment is not rational but customary and separable. Then the author explains the term 'khalaf' (disagreement): the disagreement over idrak is based on the earlier disagreement over speech, hearing, and sight. Those who affirm those attributes by rational proof (perfection) affirm idrak; those who affirm them by transmitted proof deny idrak because no transmission exists. Finally, the author presents the position of suspension (waqf) held by some theologians due to conflicting evidence, and notes it is the safest view.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Perception (idrak) necessarily entails physical contact with the object.
Correction: The passage argues that connection is only customary, not rationally necessary, and Allah's perception is without connection.

Checkpoint

A) Because it is a transmitted proof from revelation
B) Because it is a perfection, and the opposite would be deficiency
C) Because it is rationally entailed by other attributes
D) Because all theologians agree on it

Key Takeaway
The attribute of idrak is affirmed by rational proof of perfection, but the objection from entailment of connection is refuted by distinguishing customary from rational, leading some scholars to suspend judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You affirm that Allah perceives all things, including your hidden thoughts and private actions. Does this reality make you more conscious of His presence in your daily life, or do you still act as if no one sees? How can you train yourself to live with a deeper sense of His perception?
?
Allah's perception is without connection or need; He is not affected by what He perceives. Yet you often worship Him as if your actions somehow benefit or please Him in a way that adds to Him. How does the truth of His self-sufficiency challenge your motivations in worship?
?
The scholars suspended judgment on this attribute due to conflicting evidence, teaching humility in the face of divine matters. In your own faith, do you demand clear answers where Allah has not given them? How can you embrace intellectual humility and trust that silence on some matters is itself a form of divine wisdom?

The Attribute of Life and the Seven Substantive Attributes
Sanusi lists the seven substantive attributes and clarifies the grammatical status of 'Hayy'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute 'Hayy' (Living) must be treated as an independent predicate rather than a conjunct of existence in the theological formulation.

Core Idea
Every divine attribute has its own logical status – 'Hayy' is not a mere appendix.

Sanusi introduces a new section on the seven substantive attributes (al-sifat al-ma'nawiyya). He lists them and immediately clarifies a potential misunderstanding: the word 'Hayy' cannot be read as a simple conjunct of 'existence'. Instead, it requires its own predicate structure. This lesson unpacks that grammatical reasoning and its theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and the list of attributes
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the list of attributes that begins with 'Hayy'. Then read the translation. Observe the author's immediate grammatical comment.
The list is part of a verse.
2
Understand the grammatical issue
The author argues that 'Hayy' cannot be a conjunct of 'existence' because that would imply a corrupt meaning. Ask why that interpretation fails.
Hint: Allah is the Living, so saying 'necessary for Him is Living' is problematic.
3
Learn the correct parsing
The author states that 'Hayy' must be a predicate of a deleted subject, with an implied 'fa'. Understand the estimation: 'Where life is necessary for Him, He is Living.'
This keeps the attribute as a direct description of Allah.
4
Connect to the broader context
Notice that this grammatical clarification is part of the author's method to prevent theological errors. The seven attributes are not additional entities but descriptions of Allah.
This lesson only covers the first attribute; others will follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
د. الصفات المعنوية سبع]
[١. كونه حيا]
1 - حَيٌّ عَلِيمٌ قادِرٌ مُرِيدُ سَمِعْ بَصِيرٌ مَا يَشَايُرِيدُ) قوله : ( حَيٌّ) لا يصح أن يكون معطوفاً على الوجود بحذف حرف العطف؛ لأنه ينحل المعنى، وواجب له حيٌّ ، وهذا فاسد لأن الله تعالى هو الحي، فتعين أن يكون خبراً لمبتدأ محذوف مقرون بالفاء والتقدير : وحيث وجبت له الحياة فهو حيّ، والذي ذكره المصنف في شرحه :
D. The seven substantive attributes.
[1. His being alive.]
1 – Living, Knowing, Powerful, Willing, Hearing, Seeing, [and] whatever He wills He wills. His saying: (Living) – it is not correct that it is conjoined to existence by dropping the conjunction; because the meaning would dissolve: 'and necessary for Him is Living' – and this is corrupt, because Allah, Exalted, is the Living. So it must be a predicate of a deleted subject connected with the fa, and the estimation: Where life is necessary for Him, He is Living. And what the author mentioned in his commentary:
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section: the seven substantive attributes (al-sifat al-ma'nawiyya). The author gives the first attribute, 'hayy' (Living), as part of a verse listing the essential attributes: Living, Knowing, Powerful, Willing, Hearing, Seeing, and [whatever He wills He wills]. Then the author provides a grammatical clarification: the word 'hayy' cannot be interpreted as a conjunct of 'existence' with the conjunction omitted, because that would yield a corrupt meaning ('and necessary for Him is Living'). Rather, it is a predicate of a deleted subject, with an implied fa, meaning: 'Where life is necessary for Him, He is Living.' The passage ends citing the author's own commentary, which is cut off in the OCR.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'Hayy' can be considered a mere conjunct of the attribute of existence, with the conjunction omitted.
Correction: The author shows that this would result in a corrupt meaning ('and necessary for Him is Living'), implying that life is a separate necessary entity. Actually, Allah is the Living, so 'Hayy' must be a direct predicate.

Checkpoint
Why can 'hayy' not be treated as a conjunct of 'existence' with the conjunction omitted?
A) Because it would imply a temporal beginning
B) Because it would make the meaning 'and necessary for Him is Living', which is corrupt since Allah is the Living
C) Because it breaks the rhyme of the verse
D) Because all attributes must have their own independent predicates

Key Takeaway
The attribute 'Hayy' must be understood as a direct predicate of Allah, not as an addition to existence, to maintain correct tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is Living,' do you ever imagine life as something added to Allah, or do you truly believe that His life is His very essence? How does this affect your trust in His constant awareness of you?
?
Think of a moment you felt spiritually distant. Did you doubt that Allah is truly Living and responsive? How does the corrected understanding of 'Hayy' reshape your certainty that He is intimately aware of your state right now?
?
The author warns that a careless grammatical reading could corrupt tawhid. What subtle misunderstandings in your own beliefs about Allah's attributes might need correction? Are you willing to examine them with the same rigor?

The Foundation: Rational vs. Scriptural Proof
Explains the foundational disagreement over proofs for divine attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the method of proving divine attributes (rational vs. scriptural) determines whether theologians affirm or deny the attribute of perception for Allah.

Core Idea
Your proof method decides your stance on divine perception.

The dispute over whether Allah possesses the attribute of perception is not isolated; it stems from a deeper disagreement about how to prove the attributes of speech, hearing, and sight. Some scholars rely solely on rational arguments, while others demand scriptural evidence. Understanding this foundational difference is key to grasping the three positions on idrak.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on proofs
Read the Arabic passage describing the two approaches: one using rational proof and the other using scriptural proof.
Notice the author's mention of the three prior attributes (speech, hearing, sight).
2
Identify the proof methods
The rational proof argues that a lack of these attributes would imply deficiencies in Allah, which is impossible. The scriptural proof only accepts attributes explicitly mentioned in revelation.
These methods lead to opposite conclusions about idrak.
3
Connect to the attribute of perception
See how each method directly impacts whether the attribute of perception (idrak) is affirmed or denied.
The passage explicitly states: whoever establishes the three by rational proof affirms idrak; whoever establishes them by scriptural proof denies it.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإلهيات
الواجب له تعالى لذلك الضد ; لأن علمه تعالى محيط بمتعلقاتها ; فهو كاف عنها حيث لم يرد سمع, ولا دل عليها فعله تعالى كخلق العالم; لأنه لا يتوقف عليها . وقوله : (خلف) أي : في جواب ذلك اختلاف; فهو مبتدأ خبره محذوف, وهذا الاختلاف مبني على الاختلاف في دليل الصفات الثلاثة السابقة التي هي الكلام والسمع والبصر, فمن أثبتها بالدليل العقلي وهو أنها صفات كمال فلو لم يتصف بها لا تصف بأضدادها وهي نقائص والنقص عليه تعالى محال, أثبت هذه الصفة التي هي صفة الإدراك, ومن أثبتها بالدليل السمعي المتقدم نفى الصفة المذكورة; لأنه لم يرد بها سمع .
قوله : (وعند قوم صح فيه الوقف) أي : وصح التوقف عن القول بإثبات الإدراك : ونفيه عند قوم من المتكلمين كالمقترح وابن التلمساني وبعض المتأخرين, لتعارض الأدلة, فهؤلاء القوم لا يجزمون بثبوت الإدراك كأهل القول الأول, ولا يجزمون بنفيه كأهل القول الثاني وهذا القول أسلم وأصح من القولين الأولين, وكما اختلف في الإدراك اختلف في الكون مدركاً, والأصح الوقف عن ذلك.
The divine matters. The obligatorily necessary for Him, exalted, [is] the opposite of that; because His knowledge, exalted, encompasses its objects; so it (His power?) suffices for them where no revelation has come, nor does His act, exalted, such as creating the world, indicate them; because it does not depend on them. And his saying: (khulf) i.e., in response to that is a difference; so it is a mubtada' whose khabar is omitted, and this difference is based on the difference in the proof of the three preceding attributes which are speech, hearing, and sight. So whoever establishes them by rational proof – that they are attributes of perfection, so if He were not described by them, He would be described by their opposites which are deficiencies, and deficiency upon Him, exalted, is impossible – establishes this attribute, which is the attribute of perception. And whoever establishes them by the preceding scriptural proof denies the mentioned attribute because no revelation has come concerning it. His saying: (And with a group, suspension is valid in it) i.e., and suspension of saying regarding affirming perception and denying it is valid according to a group of theologians, such as al-Muqattir, Ibn al-Tilimsani, and some later scholars, due to the conflict of proofs. So these people do not categorically affirm perception like the people of the first opinion, nor do they categorically deny it like the people of the second opinion. And this opinion is safer and sounder than the two preceding opinions. And just as they differed concerning perception, they differed concerning being one who perceives (kawnun mudrikan), and the soundest is suspension concerning that.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage deals with the attribute of idrak (perception) and the differences of opinion among theologians regarding whether Allah possesses it. The author explains that the disagreement is built upon the earlier disagreement concerning the proofs for the attributes of speech, hearing, and sight. Those who establish those three attributes by rational proof – arguing that they are attributes of perfection and that their opposites are deficiencies impossible for Allah – also affirm the attribute of idrak. Those who establish them solely by scriptural proof deny idrak because no revelation has come concerning it. Then the author mentions a third position held by some theologians, such as al-Muqattir and Ibn al-Tilimsani, who suspend judgment (waqf) regarding idrak due to conflicting proofs. This third position is considered safer and sounder. The same suspension is applicable to the attribute of being one who perceives (kawnun mudrikan). The passage thus presents three positions: affirmation, denial, and suspension.

Key Terms
الدليل العقلي
الدليل السمعي
صفة الإدراك
الكلام
السمع
البصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does one who uses rational proof for the three attributes (speech, hearing, sight) arrive at the conclusion about idrak?
A) He denies idrak because it is not mentioned in revelation.
B) He affirms idrak by analogy to the three attributes.
C) He suspends judgment due to conflicting proofs.
D) He relies solely on the act of creation.

Key Takeaway
The disagreement over idrak is rooted in the methodological choice between rational and scriptural proof for divine attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider Allah's attributes, do you find yourself relying more on rational deduction or on explicit revelation? Does one method dominate, and what might that say about your trust in your own intellect versus divine texts?
?
Are there attributes of Allah that you struggle to accept because they are not explicitly mentioned in the Qur'an or hadith, even though reason points to them? How do you reconcile your hesitation with the principle that Allah's perfection requires such attributes?
?
If the rational proof for idrak leads you to affirm it, yet you cannot fully grasp how Allah perceives, does this challenge your intellectual humility? Will you submit to the proof even when your mind cannot picture the reality, or will you let your deficiency in comprehension create doubt?

Three Positions on al-Idrak and the Validity of Suspension
Lists the three positions on idrak and endorses suspension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the three theological positions regarding Allah's attribute of perception (idrak) and understand why the position of suspension (waqf) is considered the safest.

Core Idea
When proofs conflict, suspend judgment.

After understanding the foundational dispute over proofs, we now examine the three actual positions theologians have taken on the attribute of perception. The passage presents affirmers, deniers, and a group who suspend judgment due to conflicting evidence. This third position is highlighted as the soundest.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the three positions
Read the Arabic portion that lists the three groups and their reasoning.
Notice the names: al-Muqattir and Ibn al-Tilmsani are mentioned as proponents of suspension.
2
Identify the first two positions
The first position affirms idrak, the second denies it. Remember that these stem from the two proof methods in the previous lesson.
The author does not name the proponents of these two positions here.
3
Understand the third position: suspension (waqf)
Some theologians suspend judgment because the proofs for and against idrak conflict. They do not affirm or deny categorically.
The author says this opinion is 'safer and sounder' (أسلم وأصح) than the first two.
4
Note the extension to 'being one who perceives'
The same difference applies to the attribute kawnun mudrikan (being one who perceives), and the soundest position is also suspension.

Source Text

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Suspension (waqf) means the theologian does not have an opinion.

Why do some theologians suspend judgment on the attribute of perception?

Key Takeaway
The safest position on Allah's attribute of perception, according to some theologians, is to suspend judgment due to conflicting evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a theological question about Allah where the evidence seems equally balanced, do you feel pressured to pick a side to appear certain? Are you willing to admit 'I do not know' and suspend judgment, trusting that this is safer in Allah's sight? What would it take for you to adopt the humility of waqf in your own heart?
?
The suspension position is called 'safer and sounder'. But your ego likely craves clear, definitive answers. Where in your spiritual life are you clinging to false certainty because admitting ambiguity feels like weakness? Will you honestly examine that area today and consider whether waqf might be the more faithful stance?
?
This lesson says that the safest position on Allah's perception is to suspend judgment due to conflicting proofs. Yet in your daily life, you rush to conclusions about Allah's actions, His wisdom, even His attributes. Are you willing to slow down, accept the tension, and say 'I suspend judgment on that matter because the evidence is not clear'? How would that change the way you worship and trust Him?
