Definition of Ta'alluq: Only Meaning-Attributes Have Relation
Defines ta'alluq and argues it is only for meaning-attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verifiers defined ta'alluq (relation) and why they restricted it to meaning-attributes (المعاني) alone.

Core Idea
An attribute's relation is its request for an extra matter, and only meaning-attributes have such a request.

Before listing the types of relations, the author establishes what 'relation' means in kalam. This is not a trivial definition—it settles a dispute: do relational-attributes (المعنوية) also have a relation? The verifiers say no, and they give a logical argument against it. Understanding this definition and its rationale is essential for correctly applying the categories that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on definition and dispute
Focus on the sentences from 'وعرفوا التعلق' down to 'تصلح له'. Also read the earlier part where the author mentions the dispute between the verifiers and some mutakallimun.
The dispute is about which attributes have ta'alluq.
2
Identify the definition of ta'alluq
Find the sentence that literally defines ta'alluq. Write it down in Arabic and English. Notice the key phrase 'طلب الصفة أمراً زائداً على الذات'.
3
Understand the argument against both types having relation
The author gives a reductio ad absurdum: if both meaning-attributes and relational-attributes had relation, it would lead to two effective causes on one effect (e.g., in power and being powerful) and to 'attainment of the already attained' in knowledge and being knowing. Grasp why this is impossible.
This is a classic kalam argument against multiple independent causative factors.
4
Ask: why does this matter?
Reflect on why the scope of ta'alluq is so important. Without this restriction, the classification of relations would be incoherent, leading to theological absurdities.
This connects to the lesson's objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان تعلقات الصفات تعلقات القدرة
٣٣ - فَقُدْرةٌ بِمُمْكِن تَعَلَّقَتْ بِلا تَنَاهِي مَا بِهِ تَعَلَّقَتْ
قوله : (فَقُدْرةٌ ... إلخ) أي : إذا أردت معرفة تعلقات الصفات، فأقول لك: (قدرة ... إلى آخره)، فالفاء فاء الفصيحة، ولما طوى ذيل مباحث الصفات، شرع في نشر ما لها من التعلقات .
والذي اعتمده المحققون أن التعلق للمعاني فقط، وقال بعض المتكلمين: للمعنوية، ولم يقل أحدٌ بأن التعلق للمعاني والمعنوية معاً، وإلا لزم اجتماع مؤثرين على أثر واحدٍ في القدرة والكون قادراً، والإرادة والكون مريداً، ولزم تحصيل الحاصل في العلم وكونه عالماً وهكذا الباقي، وعرفوا التعلق بأنه طلب الصفة أمراً زائداً على الذات تصلح له.
واعلم أن صفاتِ المعاني من حيث التعلق وعدمه، ومن حيث عموم التعلق للواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وخصوصه بالممكنات أو بالموجودات، أقسام أربعة : الأول : ما يتعلَّق بالممكنات ؛ وهو القدرة والإرادة ، لكن تعلُّق الأولى تعلُّق إيجاد وإعدام، وتعلُّق الثانية تعلُّق تخصيص.
والثاني: ما يتعلق بالواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وهو العلم والكلام، لكن تعلق الأولِ تعلق انكشاف، وتعلق الثاني تعلق دلالة.
والثالث : ما يتعلق بالموجودات، وهو السمع والبصر والإدراك، إن قيل به والرابع: ما لا يتعلق بشيء وهو الحياة، وقد ذكرها المصنف على هذا الترتيب كما ستراه، ومعرفة التعلقات غير واجبة على المكلَّف؛ لأنها من غوامض علم الكلام ، كما نقله الشيخ البَرَّاوي عن سيدي محمد الصغير، وذكره الشيخ الشنواني .
Explanation of the relations of attributes. The relations of power.
33 - A power relates to a possible, without limit to that which it relates.
His saying: (A power ... etc.) means: if you wish to know the relations of the attributes, I say to you: (power ... etc.), so the 'fa' is the 'fa' of eloquence. And when he folded the skirt of the discussions of attributes, he began to spread what pertains to them of relations.
And that upon which the verifiers have relied is that the relation is only for the meaning-attributes (المعاني), and some mutakallimun said: for the relational-attributes (المعنوية), and no one has said that the relation is for both the meaning-attributes and the relational-attributes together, because that would necessitate the conjunction of two effective causes on one effect in power and being powerful, and will and being willing, and would necessitate the attainment of the already attained in knowledge and being knowing, and likewise the rest. And they defined the relation as: a request by the attribute for an additional matter beyond the essence that it is suitable for.
And know that the attributes of meanings, in terms of relation and lack thereof, and in terms of the generality of relation to the necessary, the contingent, and the impossible, and its specificity to possibles or to existents, are four categories:
First: That which relates to possibles, and that is power and will, but the relation of the first is a relation of bringing into existence and annihilating, and the relation of the second is a relation of specification.
Second: That which relates to the necessary, the contingent, and the impossible, and that is knowledge and speech, but the relation of the first is a relation of disclosure, and the relation of the second is a relation of indication.
Third: That which relates to existents, and that is hearing, sight, and perception, if it is affirmed.
Fourth: That which does not relate to anything, and that is life. And the author has mentioned them in this order as you will see. And knowledge of the relations is not obligatory upon the legally responsible person, because they are among the subtleties of kalam, as narrated by al-Barrawi from Sayyidi Muhammad al-Saghir, and mentioned by al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'relation' (تعلق) of attributes and enumerates its types. It begins by introducing the section on relations of attributes, quoting the poem line about power relating to possibles. The commentary explains that the 'fa' is the 'fa' of eloquence, indicating that the author is now elaborating after previous discussion. Then the author states the scholarly consensus: relation applies only to the meaning-attributes (المعاني), i.e., the essential attributes like power, knowledge, will, etc., not to the relational attributes (المعنوية). He rejects the idea that both types have relation, as that would lead to multiple causative factors. Then he gives the definition of relation: it is a request by the attribute for an additional matter beyond the essence that it is suitable for. Finally, he classifies the four types of relation based on the objects of attributes. (1) Power and will relate to possibles, but power's relation is creative (إيجاد وإعدام) while will's is specification (تخصيص). (2) Knowledge and speech relate to the necessary, contingent, and impossible—knowledge discloses, speech indicates. (3) Hearing, sight, and perception (if affirmed) relate to existents. (4) Life has no relation at all. The author notes that knowing these relations is not obligatory, as it is a subtle matter of kalam.

Key Terms
التعلق
المعاني
المعنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that ta'alluq applies to both essential attributes (like power) and their derived properties (like being powerful).
Correction: The verifiers assert that ta'alluq is only for meaning-attributes; including relational-attributes would cause logical contradictions like having two effective causes for the same effect.

Checkpoint
According to the verifiers, which attributes have ta'alluq?
A) Only meaning-attributes (المعاني)
B) Only relational-attributes (المعنوية)
C) Both meaning-attributes and relational-attributes
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Ta'alluq is defined as the attribute's request for an extra matter beyond the essence, and it is only affirmed for meaning-attributes, not for relational-attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own attributes, do you notice that your power or knowledge often seeks something beyond yourself—a desire for more? How does this contrast with the self-sufficiency of Allah, whose attributes do not need an extra matter to be real but are purely relational? What does this teach you about your own dependency on creation?
?
The passage argues that if both meaning and relational attributes had relation, it would lead to impossibility. In your life, do you ever try to assign multiple ultimate causes to your spiritual states—attributing your faith both to your own effort and to divine grace as if they are independent? How does this lesson warn you against such dualism in tawheed?
?
Ta'alluq is defined as a 'request' by the attribute. Consider your own heart: what does it continually 'request' beyond your essence—status, comfort, validation? Are you willing to let those requests be shaped by the truth that only Allah is the object of all real relations? What would change in your daily actions if you truly believed that.

The Four Categories of Attribute Relations
Enumerates four categories of relations of meaning-attributes and notes their subtlety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four categories of relations of meaning-attributes and identify which attributes belong to each category.

Core Idea
Meaning-attributes relate to their objects in four distinct ways, from possibles to nothing at all.

Now that we know ta'alluq belongs only to meaning-attributes, the author classifies their relations based on the scope of their objects. Some attributes relate to possibles, others to all intelligible realities, others only to existents, and life remarkably has no relation at all. This classification deepens our understanding of how each divine attribute functions in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration of the four categories
Read the passage from 'واعلم أن صفاتِ المعاني...' to the end. Notice the author's careful wording: each category is defined by what the attribute relates to.
2
Identify the attributes in each category
For each category, list the attributes: first: power and will; second: knowledge and speech; third: hearing, sight, perception; fourth: life. Note the specific type of relation for each.
Power's relation is 'bringing into existence and annihilating'; will's is 'specification'.
3
Understand the objects of each category
First category relates to possibles (الممكنات); second relates to necessary, contingent, and impossible (الواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات); third to existents (الموجودات); fourth to nothing.
Knowledge's relation is 'disclosure' (انكشاف); speech's is 'indication' (دلالة).
4
Reflect on the non-obligatory note
The author concludes that knowing these relations is not obligatory for the legally responsible person because it is a subtlety of kalam. Ask yourself: why would the author include this disclaimer?
This highlights that such details are for advanced students, not general required belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان تعلقات الصفات تعلقات القدرة
٣٣ - فَقُدْرةٌ بِمُمْكِن تَعَلَّقَتْ بِلا تَنَاهِي مَا بِهِ تَعَلَّقَتْ
قوله : (فَقُدْرةٌ ... إلخ) أي : إذا أردت معرفة تعلقات الصفات، فأقول لك: (قدرة ... إلى آخره)، فالفاء فاء الفصيحة، ولما طوى ذيل مباحث الصفات، شرع في نشر ما لها من التعلقات .
والذي اعتمده المحققون أن التعلق للمعاني فقط، وقال بعض المتكلمين: للمعنوية، ولم يقل أحدٌ بأن التعلق للمعاني والمعنوية معاً، وإلا لزم اجتماع مؤثرين على أثر واحدٍ في القدرة والكون قادراً، والإرادة والكون مريداً، ولزم تحصيل الحاصل في العلم وكونه عالماً وهكذا الباقي، وعرفوا التعلق بأنه طلب الصفة أمراً زائداً على الذات تصلح له.
واعلم أن صفاتِ المعاني من حيث التعلق وعدمه، ومن حيث عموم التعلق للواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وخصوصه بالممكنات أو بالموجودات، أقسام أربعة : الأول : ما يتعلَّق بالممكنات ؛ وهو القدرة والإرادة ، لكن تعلُّق الأولى تعلُّق إيجاد وإعدام، وتعلُّق الثانية تعلُّق تخصيص.
والثاني: ما يتعلق بالواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وهو العلم والكلام، لكن تعلق الأولِ تعلق انكشاف، وتعلق الثاني تعلق دلالة.
والثالث : ما يتعلق بالموجودات، وهو السمع والبصر والإدراك، إن قيل به والرابع: ما لا يتعلق بشيء وهو الحياة، وقد ذكرها المصنف على هذا الترتيب كما ستراه، ومعرفة التعلقات غير واجبة على المكلَّف؛ لأنها من غوامض علم الكلام ، كما نقله الشيخ البَرَّاوي عن سيدي محمد الصغير، وذكره الشيخ الشنواني .
Explanation of the relations of attributes. The relations of power.
33 - A power relates to a possible, without limit to that which it relates.
His saying: (A power ... etc.) means: if you wish to know the relations of the attributes, I say to you: (power ... etc.), so the 'fa' is the 'fa' of eloquence. And when he folded the skirt of the discussions of attributes, he began to spread what pertains to them of relations.
And that upon which the verifiers have relied is that the relation is only for the meaning-attributes (المعاني), and some mutakallimun said: for the relational-attributes (المعنوية), and no one has said that the relation is for both the meaning-attributes and the relational-attributes together, because that would necessitate the conjunction of two effective causes on one effect in power and being powerful, and will and being willing, and would necessitate the attainment of the already attained in knowledge and being knowing, and likewise the rest. And they defined the relation as: a request by the attribute for an additional matter beyond the essence that it is suitable for.
And know that the attributes of meanings, in terms of relation and lack thereof, and in terms of the generality of relation to the necessary, the contingent, and the impossible, and its specificity to possibles or to existents, are four categories:
First: That which relates to possibles, and that is power and will, but the relation of the first is a relation of bringing into existence and annihilating, and the relation of the second is a relation of specification.
Second: That which relates to the necessary, the contingent, and the impossible, and that is knowledge and speech, but the relation of the first is a relation of disclosure, and the relation of the second is a relation of indication.
Third: That which relates to existents, and that is hearing, sight, and perception, if it is affirmed.
Fourth: That which does not relate to anything, and that is life. And the author has mentioned them in this order as you will see. And knowledge of the relations is not obligatory upon the legally responsible person, because they are among the subtleties of kalam, as narrated by al-Barrawi from Sayyidi Muhammad al-Saghir, and mentioned by al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'relation' (تعلق) of attributes and enumerates its types. It begins by introducing the section on relations of attributes, quoting the poem line about power relating to possibles. The commentary explains that the 'fa' is the 'fa' of eloquence, indicating that the author is now elaborating after previous discussion. Then the author states the scholarly consensus: relation applies only to the meaning-attributes (المعاني), i.e., the essential attributes like power, knowledge, will, etc., not to the relational attributes (المعنوية). He rejects the idea that both types have relation, as that would lead to multiple causative factors. Then he gives the definition of relation: it is a request by the attribute for an additional matter beyond the essence that it is suitable for. Finally, he classifies the four types of relation based on the objects of attributes. (1) Power and will relate to possibles, but power's relation is creative (إيجاد وإعدام) while will's is specification (تخصيص). (2) Knowledge and speech relate to the necessary, contingent, and impossible—knowledge discloses, speech indicates. (3) Hearing, sight, and perception (if affirmed) relate to existents. (4) Life has no relation at all. The author notes that knowing these relations is not obligatory, as it is a subtle matter of kalam.

الممكنات

المستحيلات
الموجودات
إيجاد وإعدام
تخصيص
انكشاف
دلالة
غوامض علم الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that life also has a relation, like the other attributes, or that all attributes relate to the same kind of objects.
Correction: Life has no relation at all, and each attribute relates to a specific domain: power/will to possibles, knowledge/speech to all modal categories, hearing/sight/perception to existents.

Checkpoint
Which attribute has no relation to anything?
A) Power
B) Knowledge
C) Life
D) Will

Key Takeaway
Meaning-attributes are classified into four categories of relation: to possibles (power, will), to all modal categories (knowledge, speech), to existents (hearing, sight, perception), and none (life).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage tells you that life has no relation to anything—God’s life is self-sufficient. How does this truth challenge your tendency to find your identity and worth in relationships, achievements, or what others think of you? What would it look like for you to root your sense of self entirely in God’s self-sufficient life?
?
Consider that God’s power relates only to possibles, not to impossibles. When you make duʿā’, do you sometimes ask for what is logically impossible (e.g., a contradiction), or do you trust God’s power within the realm of possibility? How can this understanding refine your dua and your reliance on God’s wisdom?

Power's Relation to Possibles: Eligibility vs Actual
Explains power's relation to possibles and introduces the eligibility/actual distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how divine power relates to all possibles, including those that will never occur, through the concept of eligibility relation.

Core Idea
Divine power relates to every possible, but to those that never occur, it relates by eligibility, not actuality.

This passage clarifies a nuance in the doctrine of divine power. While power extends to all possibles, how does it relate to things that Allah knows will never happen? The answer distinguishes between two types of relation: eligibility and actual. Understanding this preserves both divine power and foreknowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the source text and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms and the flow of the argument.
2
Understand the definition of 'possible'
The passage defines 'possible' as that whose existence or non-existence is not necessary in itself, even if it becomes necessary due to another. Grasp this before moving on.
This definition is crucial for the distinction that follows.
3
Identify the two types of relation
Find where the text introduces the distinction between 'talluq suluhi' (eligibility relation) and 'talluq tanjizi' (actual relation). Understand why the latter cannot apply to things that Allah knows will not occur.
The key phrase: 'تعلق صلوحي لا تنجيزي'.
4
See the reconciliation of two opinions
Notice how the author uses this distinction to reconcile the view that such things are within power and the view that they are not. The first opinion is correct if interpreted as eligibility.
This shows the practical theological importance of the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بِمُمْكِن تَعَلَّقَتْ الجار والمجرور متعلق بالفعل بعده، وإنما قدمه عليه لإفادة الحصر، فكأنه قال: لا تتعلق إلا بممكن؛ أي بكل ممكن، فالمراد العموم لأن النكرة في سياق الإثبات قد تعم، كما في قوله تعالى : عَلِمَتْ نَفْسٌ مَا أَحْضَرَتْ) التكوير : ١٤]؛ أي: كل نفس، فالقدرة متعلقة بجميع الممكنات؛ لأنه لو خرج ممكن عن تعلقها لزم منه العجز، وهو محال عليه تعالى.
في ذاته (1)
والمراد بالممكن : ما لا يجب وجوده ولا عدمه لذاته، ولو وجب وجوده أو عدمه لغيره، فالذي تعلَّق علمه تعالى بوجوده من الممكنات، فهو وإن كان ممكناً لكن وجب وجوده لغيره، كإيمانِ مَنْ علم الله إيمانه، والذي تعلق علمه تعالى بعدم وجوده، فهو وإن كان ممكناً في ذاته لكن وجب عدم وجوده لغيره، كإيمانِ مَنْ علم الله عدم إيمانه كأبي جهل، لكن تعلق القدرة بالذي تعلق علم الله بعدم وجوده.. تعلق صلوحي لا تنجيزي، وإلا لانقلب العلم جهلاً، وهو محال، وبذلك يجمع بين القولين، فالقول بأنه من متعلقاتِ القدرة محمول على أنه من متعلقاتها باعتبار التعلقِ
(1) في (ط): (علم).
His saying: (in a possible relates) — the preposition and its object are connected to the verb after it, and he advanced it over it to indicate restriction, as if he said: it does not relate except to a possible, i.e., to every possible. So the intended meaning is generality, because the indefinite noun in the context of affirmation may be general, as in His statement, exalted: 'Every soul knows what it has brought' (al-Takwir:14), i.e., every soul. So power is related to all possibles, because if a possible were outside its relation, impotence would follow, and that is impossible for Him, exalted.
In His essence (1)
And the meaning of 'possible' is: that whose existence and non-existence are not necessary in itself, even if its existence or non-existence becomes necessary due to another. So that whose existence His knowledge, exalted, has encompassed from among the possibles, even though it is possible, its existence becomes necessary due to another, like the faith of one whom Allah knows to have faith. And that whose non-existence His knowledge, exalted, has encompassed, even though it is possible in itself, its non-existence becomes necessary due to another, like the faith of one whom Allah knows will not have faith, like Abu Jahl. But the relation of power to that whose non-existence Allah has encompassed is a relation of eligibility (صلاحي) not actual (تنجيزي), otherwise knowledge would turn into ignorance, and that is impossible. And by that, reconciliation is made between the two sayings. So the saying that it is among the relations of power is interpreted as being among its relations in terms of the relation (of eligibility).
(1) In (T): (علم).
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed analysis of how power (قدرة) relates to possibles, addressing a potential objection. The line under comment is 'قدرة بممكن تعلقت' meaning 'power relates to a possible.' The author emphasizes that the preposition and its object are advanced to indicate restriction: power relates only to possibles, and to every possible. The indefinite 'بممكن' is interpreted as general because it is in an affirmative context. He then clarifies what 'possible' means: something whose existence and non-existence are not necessary in themselves, even if they become necessary due to an external factor. For example, the faith of someone whom Allah knows will believe is possible in itself but becomes necessary due to Allah's knowledge. Similarly, the unbelief of someone like Abu Jahl is possible in itself but becomes necessary due to Allah's knowledge of its non-occurrence. However, power's relation to that which Allah knows will not occur is a relation of eligibility (تعلق صلاحي) not actual (تنجيزي). If power were related actually, it would imply that Allah's knowledge changes, which is impossible. This reconciles two opinions: one holding that such things are within power, the other that they are not. The first opinion is correct if interpreted as a relation of eligibility.

ممكن
تعلق صلاحي
تعلق تنجيزي
العجز
انقلاب العلم جهلاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that divine power cannot relate to things that will never happen, because they are impossible.
Correction: They are not impossible; they are possible in themselves. Power relates to them by eligibility, preserving divine foreknowledge.

Checkpoint

A) With an actual relation (تنجيزي)
B) With a relation of eligibility (صلاحي)

D) With a relation of necessity

Key Takeaway
Divine power relates to all possibles, but to those that will never occur, it is a relation of eligibility, not actuality, preserving divine foreknowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage explains that for those whose non-existence is known by God, His power relates to them only by eligibility, not actuality. This means that although something is possible in itself, it will never happen because God knows it won't. Consider your own faith: do you truly believe that your faith is a gift from God, and that He knows whether you will remain faithful until death? How does the reality that your entire spiritual journey is encompassed by divine knowledge change how you approach your daily acts of worship? Are you actively choosing to turn your potential faith into actual faith, or are you complacent? Urgently ask yourself: What concrete step will you take today to ensure that the possibility of your faith becomes an actuality?
?
The author uses the example of Abu Jahl to illustrate that even his unbelief, though possible in itself, was necessary due to God's knowledge. This teaches us that God's power and knowledge are perfectly consistent. Think about a time you doubted God's wisdom because something bad happened to you. Can you now see that even that event was within the realm of God's power, but He chose not to bring about a different outcome for a reason you may not understand? How can this lesson fortify your trust in God when you face trials? Commit to recite the lesson's principle whenever you feel doubt: 'His power relates to all possibles, but to those that never occur, it is a relation of eligibility, not actuality, preserving His knowledge.'
?
The distinction between eligibility and actuality is not just philosophical; it has a practical impact on how we understand our own intentions. You may intend to do good deeds, but only those that Allah knows will happen become actual. Does this realization humble you? Does it make you turn to Allah more often, asking Him to grant you success in acting upon your good intentions? Write down one intention you have had for a long time but never acted upon. Today, decide to turn that eligibility into actuality, relying on Allah's power.

Four Types of Divine Attributes by Attachment
The author classifies four types of divine attributes of meanings by attachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four categories of divine attributes of meanings based on what they attach to, and why knowing these details is not obligatory for every Muslim.

Core Idea
Divine attributes attach to different realities—some to possibles, some to all things, some to existents, and life to nothing.

The science of kalam carefully classifies divine attributes to avoid misunderstanding Allah's nature. This passage introduces a key classification: the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-maʿānī) are divided into four types depending on what they 'attach' to. Understanding this classification deepens theological precision, yet the author notes that such details are not required for every believer—they are part of the subtleties of kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a sense of the author's style and the flow of the classification. Then read the translation carefully.
Notice the definition of attachment at the beginning.
2
Identify the four divisions
List the four categories mentioned: those attaching to possible things, those attaching to necessary/possible/impossible, those attaching to existents, and that which attaches to nothing.
Each category includes specific attributes.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why this classification matters. It helps us understand how divine attributes relate to creation and to Allah's essence.
The note about non-obligatory knowledge shows the depth of kalam.
4
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you can recall which attribute attaches to nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإلهيات الحاصل في العلم وكونه عالماً وهكذا الباقي، وعرفوا التعلق بأنه طلب الصفة أمراً زائداً على الذات تصلح له. واعلم أن صفاتِ المعاني من حيث التعلق وعدمه، ومن حيث عموم التعلق للواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وخصوصه بالممكنات أو بالموجودات، أقسام أربعة : الأول : ما يتعلَّق بالممكنات ؛ وهو القدرة والإرادة ، لكن تعلُّق الأولى تعلُّق إيجاد وإعدام، وتعلُّق الثانية تعلُّق تخصيص. والثاني: ما يتعلق بالواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وهو العلم والكلام، لكن تعلق الأولِ تعلق انكشاف، وتعلق الثاني تعلق دلالة. والثالث : ما يتعلق بالموجودات، وهو السمع والبصر والإدراك، إن قيل به والرابع: ما لا يتعلق بشيء وهو الحياة، وقد ذكرها المصنف على هذا الترتيب كما ستراه، ومعرفة التعلقات غير واجبة على المكلَّف؛ لأنها من غوامض علم الكلام، كما نقله الشيخ البراوي عن سيدي محمد الصغير، وذكره الشيخ الشنواني.
The divine matters: what is obtained in knowledge and His being knowing, and likewise the rest. And they defined attachment (al-ta'alluq) as the attribute's seeking something additional to the essence that is suitable for it. And know that the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-maʿānī) from the perspective of attachment and non-attachment, and from the perspective of generality of attachment to necessary, possible, and impossible things, and its specificity to possible things or to existents, are four divisions: The first: what attaches to possible things – and it is power and will, but the attachment of the first is attachment of bringing into existence and annihilating, and the attachment of the second is attachment of specification. The second: what attaches to necessary, possible, and impossible things – and it is knowledge and speech, but the attachment of the first is attachment of disclosure, and the attachment of the second is attachment of indication. The third: what attaches to existents – and it is hearing, sight, and perception, if it be said. And the fourth: what does not attach to anything – and it is life. And the author (al-muṣannif) mentioned them in this order as you will see. And knowledge of the attachments is not obligatory upon the legally responsible person (al-mukallaf), because it is among the subtleties of the science of kalam, as transmitted by al-Shaykh al-Barrawi from Sayyidī Muḥammad al-Ṣaghīr, and mentioned by al-Shaykh al-Shanwānī.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a classification of divine attributes. It begins by defining attachment (ta'alluq) as the attribute's seeking something additional to the essence that is suitable for it. Then it states that the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-maʿānī) are divided into four types based on what they attach to: (1) those attaching to possible things (power and will) – power's attachment is bringing into existence and annihilating, will's attachment is specification; (2) those attaching to necessary, possible, and impossible things (knowledge and speech) – knowledge's attachment is disclosure, speech's attachment is indication; (3) those attaching to existents (hearing, sight, and perception, if accepted); (4) that which does not attach to anything (life). The author notes that the author of the matn (Jawharat al-Tawhid) mentioned them in this order. Finally, it clarifies that knowledge of these attachments is not obligatory for the mukallaf because they are among the subtleties of kalam, citing authorities.

?

Does this make you turn to Him in constant humility and fear, or do you live as if your existence is secure? What change will you make today because of this truth?

Power Attaches Only to Possibles
Sanusi explains the restriction of power to possibles and defines possible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine power attaches only to possible things and how 'possible' is defined in kalam, including its dependence on divine knowledge and the notion of necessity by another.

Core Idea
Divine power only attaches to possibles because they alone can be either created or left uncreated.

The theological tradition affirms that God's power is unrestricted, yet it does not attach to everything without distinction. This passage from Sanusi's commentary clarifies the fundamental principle: power attaches only to possible things. Understanding what 'possible' means in this context is essential before exploring how God's power relates to events that never happen.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening lines
The passage starts by explaining the phrase 'to a possible it attached' from the matn. Notice how the preposition is advanced for restriction, meaning power attaches only to possibles.
The author uses the example from the Quran to illustrate generality.
2
Understand the definition of possible
Possible (al-mumkin) is defined as that whose existence and non-existence are not necessary in itself. However, it may become necessary due to another, like the faith of those whose faith God knows.
This nuance is important for understanding how divine knowledge relates to power.
3
Reflect on the examples
Consider the examples of the faithful and Abu Jahl. Even though Abu Jahl's faith is impossible in reality, it remains a possible in itself – its non-existence is necessary due to divine knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بِمُمْكِن تَعَلَّقَتْ الجار والمجرور متعلق بالفعل بعده، وإنما قدمه عليه لإفادة الحصر، فكأنه قال: لا تتعلق إلا بممكن؛ أي بكل ممكن، فالمراد العموم لأن النكرة في سياق الإثبات قد تعم، كما في قوله تعالى : عَلِمَتْ نَفْسٌ مَا أَحْضَرَتْ) التكوير : ١٤]؛ أي: كل نفس، فالقدرة متعلقة بجميع الممكنات؛ لأنه لو خرج ممكن عن تعلقها لزم منه العجز، وهو محال عليه تعالى. (1) في ذاته والمراد بالممكن : ما لا يجب وجوده ولا عدمه لذاته، ولو وجب وجوده أو عدمه لغيره، فالذي تعلَّق علمه تعالى بوجوده من الممكنات، فهو وإن كان ممكناً لكن وجب وجوده لغيره، كإيمانِ مَنْ علم الله إيمانه، والذي تعلق علمه تعالى بعدم وجوده، فهو وإن كان ممكناً في ذاته لكن وجب عدم وجوده لغيره، كإيمانِ مَنْ علم الله عدم إيمانه كأبي جهل، لكن تعلق القدرة بالذي تعلق علم الله بعدم وجوده.. تعلق صلوحي لا تنجيزي، وإلا لانقلب العلم جهلاً، وهو محال، وبذلك يجمع بين القولين، فالقول بأنه من متعلقاتِ القدرة محمول على أنه من متعلقاتها باعتبار التعلقِ الصلوحي ، والقول بأنه ليس مِنْ متعلقاتِ القدرة محمول على أنه ليس من متعلقاتها باعتبار التعلَّقِ التنجيزي. وعُلم من ذلك أن للقدرة تعلقين : تعلَّقاً صلوحيا قديماً : وهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام فيما لا يزال. وتنجيزيا حادثاً وهو الإيجاد والإعدام بها بالفعل، وهذا على سبيل الإجمال؛ وأمَّا على سبيل التفصيل فلها تعلقات سبعة، وقد تقدم بيانها . وخرج بالممكن الواجب والمستحيلُ، فلا تتعلَّقُ القدرة بهما؛ لأنَّها إن تعلَّقت بوجود الواجب لزم تحصيل الحاصل، وإن تعلّقت بعدمه لزم انقلاب حقيقة الواجب؛ فإِنَّ حقيقته ما لا يقبل العدم، وإن تعلَّقتْ بالمستحيل فعلى العكس من ذلك.
His saying: 'To a possible it attached' – the preposition and noun are attached to the verb after it, and he advanced it over the verb to indicate restriction, as if he said: It attaches only to a possible; i.e., to every possible, so the intended meaning is generality because the indefinite in the context of affirmation may be general, as in His saying: 'Every soul knows what it has brought forth' (81:14); i.e., every soul. So power is attached to all possible things, because if a possible were excluded from its attachment, powerlessness (al-ʿajz) would necessarily follow, and that is impossible for Him, exalted is He. (1) In His essence. And what is meant by possible (al-mumkin) is that whose existence and non-existence are not necessary in itself, even if its existence or non-existence is necessary due to another. So that whose existence His knowledge, exalted, has attached to from among the possibles – even though it is possible, its existence is necessary due to another, like the faith of one whose faith God knows. And that whose non-existence His knowledge has attached to – even though it is possible in itself, its non-existence is necessary due to another, like the faith of one whose lack of faith God knows, such as Abu Jahl. But the attachment of power to that to which God's knowledge of its non-existence is attached is an aptitudinal (ṣulūḥī) attachment, not an actual (tanjīzī) one; otherwise knowledge would turn into ignorance, and that is impossible. And by that, the two sayings are reconciled. For the saying that it is among the attachments of power is interpreted as it being among its attachments in terms of aptitudinal attachment, and the saying that it is not among the attachments of power is interpreted as it not being among its attachments in terms of actual attachment. And from that it is known that power has two attachments: an eternal aptitudinal attachment – which is its suitability in pre-eternity for bringing into existence and annihilating in what will be; and a temporal actual attachment – which is the actual bringing into existence and annihilating by it. And this is in summary. As for in detail, it has seven attachments, and their explanation has preceded. And by possible, the necessary (al-wājib) and the impossible (al-mustaḥīl) are excluded. So power does not attach to them, because if it attached to the existence of the necessary, obtaining the obtained (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil) would follow; and if it attached to its non-existence, a change in the reality of the necessary would follow, for its reality is that it does not admit non-existence. And if it attached to the impossible, the opposite of that applies.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a proof and classification concerning divine power (qudra). It begins by explaining the phrase 'to a possible it attached' from the matn, showing that power attaches only to possible things (mumkināt) – the preposition is advanced for restriction. It then defines possible as that whose existence and non-existence are not necessary in themselves, even if they become necessary by another (e.g., the faith of a person known by God to be faithful becomes necessary but remains possible in itself). The distinction between aptitudinal (ṣulūḥī) and actual (tanjīzī) attachment is introduced to reconcile two positions: power has an aptitudinal attachment to things that are known not to happen (like Abu Jahl's faith), but not an actual attachment; otherwise God's knowledge would be false. Then it states that power has two types of attachment: eternal aptitudinal (suitability in pre-eternity) and temporal actual (actual creation). The seven detailed attachments are mentioned as previously known. Finally, it excludes the necessary (wājib) and impossible (mustaḥīl) from power's attachment, giving reasons: attaching to the necessary would be obtaining the already obtained, and attaching to its non-existence would change its reality; for the impossible, the opposite (similar reasoning).

Key Terms
القدرة
الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the restriction 'to a possible it attached' indicate about divine power?
A) Power attaches to all things, including the impossible.
B) Power attaches only to possible things.
C) Power attaches only to existing things.
D) Power attaches to possible and necessary things.

Key Takeaway
In kalam, 'possible' is defined by the absence of necessity in itself, not by actual existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah's power extends to every possibility, even those that seem impossible to you? How does that affect your du'a and reliance on Him?
?
Consider something you desperately desire to happen—do you treat it as if its existence is necessary from itself, forgetting that it is only possible and depends entirely on Allah's will?
?
Abu Jahl's disbelief was possible in itself but necessary due to Allah's knowledge. Are there sins in your life that you excuse as 'inevitable' but are merely possibilities that you have chosen to actualize? What would change if you truly believed they are not necessary?

Divine Attributes

Two Types of Power's Attachment and Exclusion of Necessary and Impossible
Sanusi distinguishes two types of attachment and excludes necessary/impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between aptitudinal and actual attachment of divine power, and why power does not attach to the necessary or impossible.

Core Idea
Power's attachment to what will never happen is aptitudinal, not actual.

In reconciling theological debates about whether power attaches to events that never occur, Sanusi introduces a crucial distinction: power has two types of attachment. This passage explains that distinction and also clarifies why the necessary and impossible lie outside power's scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of attachment
The passage introduces two attachments: aptitudinal (suluhi) and actual (tanjizi). Aptitudinal is the eternal suitability to create or annihilate, while actual is the temporal action.
This distinction reconciles the debate about power attaching to events that never happen.
2
Understand the reconciliation
The two sayings are reconciled by interpreting one as referring to aptitudinal attachment and the other to actual attachment.
3
Note the exclusion of necessary and impossible
Power does not attach to the necessary (wajib) or impossible (mustahil). Attaching to the necessary would be obtaining the obtained or changing its reality; for the impossible, the opposite.
This shows power is limited by logical possibility.

Source Text

(1) في ذاته والمراد بالممكن : ما لا يجب وجوده ولا عدمه لذاته، ولو وجب وجوده أو عدمه لغيره، فالذي تعلَّق علمه تعالى بوجوده من الممكنات، فهو وإن كان ممكناً لكن وجب وجوده لغيره، كإيمانِ مَنْ علم الله إيمانه، والذي تعلق علمه تعالى بعدم وجوده، فهو وإن كان ممكناً في ذاته لكن وجب عدم وجوده لغيره، كإيمانِ مَنْ علم الله عدم إيمانه كأبي جهل، لكن تعلق القدرة بالذي تعلق علم الله بعدم وجوده.. تعلق صلوحي لا تنجيزي، وإلا لانقلب العلم جهلاً، وهو محال، وبذلك يجمع بين القولين، فالقول بأنه من متعلقاتِ القدرة محمول على أنه من متعلقاتها باعتبار التعلقِ الصلوحي ، والقول بأنه ليس مِنْ متعلقاتِ القدرة محمول على أنه ليس من متعلقاتها باعتبار التعلَّقِ التنجيزي. وعُلم من ذلك أن للقدرة تعلقين : تعلَّقاً صلوحيا قديماً : وهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام فيما لا يزال. وتنجيزيا حادثاً وهو الإيجاد والإعدام بها بالفعل، وهذا على سبيل الإجمال؛ وأمَّا على سبيل التفصيل فلها تعلقات سبعة، وقد تقدم بيانها . وخرج بالممكن الواجب والمستحيلُ، فلا تتعلَّقُ القدرة بهما؛ لأنَّها إن تعلَّقت بوجود الواجب لزم تحصيل الحاصل، وإن تعلّقت بعدمه لزم انقلاب حقيقة الواجب؛ فإِنَّ حقيقته ما لا يقبل العدم، وإن تعلَّقتْ بالمستحيل فعلى العكس من ذلك.

Why does power not attach to the necessary (wajib)?
A) Because it is not a possible.

C) Because it would cause deficiency in God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you truly believed that God's power never attaches to the impossible because it is not truly possible, would your anxiety about the future decrease? In what area of your life are you demanding that God do something that might be impossible in His knowledge, and how can you surrender that to His mercy and wisdom?
?
The passage warns against thinking that power attaches to the necessary because it would be redundant (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil). Have you ever expected God to act in a way that would be redundant or contradict His own nature? How does this lesson teach you to align your expectations with the reality of who God is?

The Unlimitedness of Divine Power's Objects and the Poetic Issue
Sanusi clarifies that the objects of power are unlimited, provides Quranic evidence, and resolves a potential poetic redundancy in the line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that while the possible objects of Allah's power are unlimited in general (e.g., ever-renewing delights of Paradise), actual existing events are finite, and you will see how a potential poetic redundancy in the poem is resolved.

Core Idea
Divine power attaches to all possible things without limit, but actual events are finite.

This passage tackles two interconnected points: first, the meaning of 'without limit' when describing the objects of divine power, and second, a subtle poetic issue that might appear as redundancy. Understanding both clarifies that Allah's power is all-encompassing, yet the actualization of events is finite. The author also presents two valid interpretations of the verse to avoid any poetic flaw.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the main claim
The passage explains that the objects of power are not limited, using the delights of Paradise as an example of endless renewal, while noting that actual external events are finite.
Notice the distinction between possible objects (limitless) and actual existents (finite).
2
Examine the scriptural evidence
Two Quranic verses are cited as proof that Allah's power covers everything (every possible). Note the interpretation of 'everything' as 'every possible'.
The verses are 2:284 and 25:2.
3
Address the poetic issue
The author refutes a claim of īṭāʾ (excessive repetition) in the line of poetry, offering two valid interpretations: either the line is from complete rajaz, or the two instances refer to actual vs. aptitudinal attachment.
The author rejects an explanation based on affirmative vs negative contexts.
4
Understand two scholarly interpretations
The gloss presents two views on what 'without limit' means: (a) an endless future series (muḥashshī) and (b) general coverage (Shaykh ʿAbd al-Salām). The latter better fits the Quranic proof.
Al-Amīr's gloss explains that limitlessness means power does not stop at a subset of possibles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : بِلا تَنَاهِي مَا بِهِ تَعَلَّقَتْ ((1)) أي : الممكن الذي تعلقت به القدرة متلبس بعدم التناهي، فمتعلقات القدرة لا تنتهي إلى حد ونهاية؛ إذ منها نعيم الجنان، وهو متجدد شيئاً فشيئاً ،وهكذا، وأما ما وُجد في الخارج من الممكن فهو متناه؛ لأنَّ كلَّ ما حصره الوجود من الممكن فهو متناه لاستحالة حوادث لا نهاية لها، ويدلُّ على عدم تناهي متعلقات القدرة قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَاللهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرُ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٨٤] ، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ لَقَدِيرًا ﴾ [الفرقان: ۱۲؛ أي: كلُّ شيء ممكن في الآيتين. واعلم أنه لا إيطاءَ في البيت ؛ لأنَّ الصحيح أنَّها مِنْ كامل الرجز، على أنه يصح حمل الأول على التنجيزي، والثاني على الصلوحي ، وأما كونُ الأول في حيز الإثبات والثاني في حيز التفي، فلا يُلتفتُ إليه وإن ذكره المصنف في شرحه) . (۱) قوله: (بلا) تناهي ... إلخ) مشى المحشّي على أن معناه أن المتعلقات لا نهاية لها في جانب أنه ما المستقبل، بمعنى من ممكن يقع في المستقبل إلا وبعده ممكن، وهكذا من غير آخر في الاستقبال، وعلى هذا فالاستدلال بالآيتين على عدم التناهي غير ظاهر؛ لأنَّهما إنما دلّا على تعلق القدرة بجميع الممكنات، وأما أن الممكنات متناهية أو لا، فلا دلالة لهما على ذلك، ومشى الشيخ عبد السلام على أن معنى عدم التناهي عموم تعلق القدرة لجميع الممكنات، حيث صوّر عدم التناهي بألا يخرج شيءٌ من الممكنات عن القدرة وعلى هذا فالاستدلال بالآيتين ظاهر، ومعنى عدم التناهي حينئذ كما ذكره الأمير في الحاشية» أن القدرة لا تنتهي عند طائفة الممكنات بأن تتعلَّق بها دون غيرها من الممكنات . انتهى أجهوري. من
His saying: 'Without limit what it attaches to' – i.e., the possible to which power attaches is characterized by limitlessness, so the attachments of power do not come to an end or limit; for among them are the delights of Paradise, which are renewed little by little, and so on. As for what exists externally from the possible, it is finite; because everything that existence encompasses from the possible is finite due to the impossibility of infinite events. And the evidence for the limitlessness of power's attachments is His saying: 'And Allah is over all things competent' (2:284), and His saying: 'And He created everything and determined it with [precise] determination' (25:2) – i.e., every possible thing in both verses. And know that there is no īṭāʾ (excessive repetition) in the line; because the correct view is that it is from the complete rajaz, although it is valid to interpret the first as actual (tanjīzī) and the second as aptitudinal (ṣulūḥī). As for the first being in the affirmative and the second in the negative, it is not to be heeded even if the author mentioned it in his commentary. (1) His saying: '(Without) limit... etc.' – the commentator (al-muḥashshī) held that its meaning is that the attachments have no end on the side of the future, i.e., no possible occurs in the future except that after it there is another possible, and so on without end in the future. On this basis, the inference from the two verses for limitlessness is not apparent, because they only indicate power's attachment to all possibles, but whether the possibles are finite or not, the two verses do not indicate that. And al-Shaykh ʿAbd al-Salām held that the meaning of limitlessness is the generality of power's attachment to all possibles, wherein limitlessness is depicted by nothing from the possibles being outside power. On this basis, the inference from the two verses is apparent. And the meaning of limitlessness then, as mentioned by al-Amīr in the gloss, is that power does not stop at a group of possibles such that it attaches to them and not to others. End of al-Ujhūrī. From.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is an explanation and a refutation of a potential objection. It begins by glossing the phrase 'without limit what it attaches to' from the poem, explaining that the possible things to which power attaches are limitless (e.g., the ever-renewing delights of Paradise). Externally existing possibles are finite due to the impossibility of infinite events. Two verses are cited as evidence: 'Allah is over all things competent' and 'He created everything and determined it with precise determination' – interpreting 'everything' as every possible. Then it addresses a potential īṭāʾ (excessive repetition) in the line of poetry, noting that it is valid as complete rajaz, and suggests interpreting the first occurrence as actual attachment and the second as aptitudinal, rejecting a previous explanation about affirmative and negative contexts. The gloss then presents two interpretations: (1) The commentator (muḥashshī) says limitlessness means an endless future series of possibles, but then the verses do not clearly prove that. (2) Shaykh ʿAbd al-Salām says it means general coverage of all possibles, which the verses do prove. The meaning of limitlessness is that power does not stop at some possibles and exclude others.

Key Terms
بلا تناهي
متعلقات القدرة
نعيم الجنان
إيطاء
كامل الرجز
التعلق التنجيزي
التعلق الصلوحي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'without limit' means all possible things are infinite in number, or that actual created things are infinite in number.
Correction: The passage clarifies that only the possible objects of power are limitless (e.g., potential future creations), but actual existents are finite due to the impossibility of an infinite regress of events. The term 'without limit' primarily means that power's attachment is general to all possibles, not that there is an infinite actual regress.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say there is no īṭāʾ (excessive repetition) in the line of poetry?
A) Because the line is from complete rajaz
B) Because the first is actual and the second aptitudinal
C) Because the contexts are different (affirmative vs negative)
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
Allah's power attaches to all possible things without limit, and a potential poetic redundancy is resolved by distinguishing between actual and aptitudinal attachment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah’s power attaches to all possible things without limit, what impossible desires are you still clinging to? Will you hand over every secret hope and fear to His unrestricted power, or will you continue to limit Him by your own finite expectations?
?
The delights of Paradise are endlessly renewed. Does your heart truly yearn for a happiness that never fades, or are you still settling for fleeting pleasures that will end? What one finite attachment must you release today to make room for the eternal?
?
The gloss distinguishes between a power that is merely possible (aptitudinal) and one that is actualized. In your relationship with Allah, are you content with just knowing the truth in theory, or will you turn that knowledge into actual obedience—today, not tomorrow?

Two Eternal Relations of Divine Power: Suluhi and Tanjizi
The author distinguishes two types of ta'alluq for divine power and refutes a third.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two eternal relational aspects of divine power: the potential relation (suluhi) and the actualizing relation (tanjizi), and why a third temporal relation is rejected.

Core Idea
God's power relates to creation eternally, not at the moment of creation.

In classical kalam, the divine attribute of power (qudra) relates to possible things before they exist. Scholars distinguish two types of this relation: one is the power's inherent suitability to specify possibilities, and the other is God's eternal determination of which possibility becomes actual. A mistaken third view posits a temporal relation at the moment of creation. This passage clarifies the correct position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own terminology and rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage is dense with technical terms like 'ta'alluq', 'suluhi', 'tanjizi'.
2
Identify the two accepted types
The passage presents two types of ta'alluq: the primordial potential relation (al-ta'alluq al-suluhi al-qadim) and the primordial actualizing relation (al-ta'alluq al-tanjizi al-qadim). Notice how each is defined.
The first is about suitability, the second about specific determination.
3
Understand the rejected third type
Some scholars proposed a temporal actualizing relation (ta'alluq tanjizi hadith) at the moment of creation. The author rejects it, stating it is not a true relation but only a manifestation (izhar) of the eternal relation.
This rejection preserves the eternity of God's power's relation.
4
Reflect on the theological import
Why does this distinction matter? It affirms that God's power is not passive or time-bound. The relation is eternal, not something that begins when the creature appears.
This connects to the doctrine of God's timelessness and omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعلقاً صلوحيًا قديماً ؛ وهو صلاحيتها في الأزل لتخصيص الممكن بالوجود أو بالعدم، وبالغنى أو بالفقر وهكذا .
وتعلُّقاً تنجيزيا قديماً ؛ وهو تخصيص الله بها أزلاً الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه من الممكنات السابقة.
وزادَ بعضُهم تعلقاً ثالثاً : وهو تعلقها بالممكن حين وجوده بالفعل، فيكون تعلقاً تنجيزيا حادثاً، والحقُّ أنَّ هذا ليس بتعلَّق، وإنما هو إظهار للتعلّق كما تقدم.
A primordial potential relation (ta'alluq suluhi qadim): it is its (the power's) suitability in pre-eternity to specify the possible (al-mumkin) with existence or non-existence, with wealth or poverty, and so on. And a primordial actualizing relation (ta'alluq tanjizi qadim): it is God's specifying in pre-eternity the possible with some of what is permissible for it from the possible things mentioned above. And some added a third relation: it is its relation to the possible at the time of its actual existence, so it would be a temporal actualizing relation (ta'alluq tanjizi hadith). But the truth is that this is not a relation; rather it is a manifestation of the relation as previously stated.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage categorizes the relational aspects (ta'alluqat) of divine power (qudra). The author defines two primary types: the first is the primordial potential relation (al-ta'alluq al-suluhi al-qadim), which is the power's suitability in eternity to specify a possible thing with existence or non-existence, etc. The second is the primordial actualizing relation (al-ta'alluq al-tanjizi al-qadim), which is God's actual determination in pre-eternity of a possible thing to a specific state among its possibilities. A third type proposed by some is a temporal actualizing relation (ta'alluq tanjizi hadith), which would be the power's relation to the possible at the moment of its actual existence. The author rejects this, stating it is not a true relation but merely a manifestation (izhar) of the relation, implying that the actualizing relation is already eternal.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's power begins to relate to a creature only at the moment of its creation.
Correction: The passage explains that the relation of God's power to possible things is eternal: both the potential suitability and the actual determination are eternal, not temporal. The moment of creation only manifests that eternal relation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rejected third type of ta'alluq for divine power?
A) Ta'alluq suluhi qadim
B) Ta'alluq tanjizi qadim
C) Ta'alluq tanjizi hadith
D) Ta'alluq suluhi hadith

Key Takeaway
Divine power has two eternal relations: the potential (suluhi) and the actualizing (tanjizi); a temporal relation at creation is merely a manifestation of the eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if God's power over your life is merely a 'temporal' reaction to your actions, or do you truly believe that His power has already specified your every state from eternity? How would your anxiety change if you fully internalized this?
?
The author calls the third relation a 'manifestation'—not a new relation. When you witness a good or bad event, do you treat it as a new decision from God, or as the unfolding of His eternal decree? Which view makes you more grateful in hardship?
?
If God's power to give or withhold existed eternally, does your reliance on Him feel as constant as that? Or do you only turn to Him when you need something 'now'? What would it look like to live with a perpetual awareness of His all-encompassing power?

Divine Knowledge Encompasses All Things: Necessaries and Impossibles
Sanusi defines the scope of divine knowledge and refutes a deviant view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine knowledge extends beyond possible things to include necessary and impossible entities, and why this distinction is important for Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Divine knowledge covers everything: what is, what must be, and what cannot be.

This lesson examines a key distinction between divine knowledge and other attributes like power and will. While power and will only relate to possibles, knowledge also encompasses the necessary and the impossible. This is a crucial point for understanding God's omniscience as taught by Imam al-Sanusi.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get its rhythm, then read the full English translation. Notice the author's flow from analogy to refutation to positive doctrine.
The passage is dense; focus on the main claims.
2
Identify the three categories of objects of knowledge
The passage states that knowledge relates to possibles (mumkinat), necessaries (wājib), and impossibles (mumtaniʿ). Mark these terms in the Arabic.
Necessaries include God's essence and attributes; impossibles include a partner or son.
3
Understand the refutation of Abu Sahl
Abu Sahl al-Su'luki held that God has multiple eternal sciences. The author argues this is impossible because an infinite regress is impossible for temporal things, but not for the eternal. Notice how this reinforces the unity of knowledge.
This refutation is a key point in the passage.
4
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites two verses: 'Allah is Knowing of everything' (49:16) and 'Knower of the unseen and the witnessed' (59:22). Understand how 'thing' means any entity, not just existents, and 'unseen/witnessed' are relative to us.
These verses support the universal scope of knowledge.
5
Reflect on the single relation of knowledge
The passage concludes that knowledge has only one type of relation: a primordial actualizing relation (taʿalluq tanjīzī qadīm). Consider why this matters for avoiding multiplicity.
This affirms the simplicity of God's knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَالعِلْمُ) معطوفٌ على قوله : (إرادة) فهو مثل القدرة أيضاً في الأمور الثلاثة تعلقه بالممكنات، وعدم تناهي متعلقاتِهِ، وإيجاب الوحدة له بإجماع مَنْ يعتد بإجماعه، فإنَّه لم يذهب أحد إلى تعدد علمه تعالى بعددِ المعلومات إلا أبو سهل الصُّعلوكيُّ فقال : بعلوم قديمةٍ لا نهاية لها، ولا يَرِدُ عليه استحالة دخول ما لا نهاية له في الوجود؛ لأنَّ الدليل إنَّما قامَ على هذه الاستحالة في الحادث دون القديم. وقوله : (لكِنْ عَمَّ ذِي) أي: لكن عمَّ العلمُ مِنْ حيثُ تعلقه هذه الممكنات التي أشعر بها عموم قوله : (بممكن) لأن المراد به العموم كما سبق، ودفع المصنف بهذا الاستدراك ما يوهمه تشبيه العلم بالقدرة مِنْ قَصْرِهِ على الممكنات كما في القدرة والإرادة، وليس كذلك، بل يتعلق أيضاً بالواجبات والمستحيلات. ولا إيطاء في كلامه لاختلاف مرجع اسمي الإشارة على أنها ليست من مشطور الرجز، بل من تامه كما تقدَّم غيرَ مرَّةٍ .
٣٥ - وَعَمَّ أَيْضاً وَاجِباً وَالمُمْتَنِعْ وَمِثلُ ذَا كَلامُهُ فَلْنَتَّبِعْ وقوله : (وَعَمَّ أَيْضاً وَاجِباً وَالمُمْتَنِعْ) أي : وشمل العلم من حيث تعلّقه الواجب العقليّ كذاته تعالى وصفاته، والممتنع العقلي كشريكه تعالى واتخاذه ولداً أو صاحبة، بمعنى أنه يعلم استحالة ذلك، ويعلم أنه لو وجد لترتب عليه من الفساد كذا وكذا. (وأيضاً) : مصدر (آضَ) إذا رجع، فمعناه رجوعاً إلى عموم العلم، فهو كما عمّ الممكنات عمَّ الواجبات والممتنعات، ويدلُّ على عموم تعلقِهِ قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاللَّهُ بِكُلِ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ ﴾ [الحجرات : ١٦] ، والمراد بالشيء: مطلق الأمر، لا خصوص الموجود، وإلا لم يطابق المُدعى، وقوله تعالى: ﴿عَلِمُ الْغَيْبِ وَالشَّهَادَة) [الحشر: ۲۲]؛ أي: ما غاب عنا وما حضر لنا، فالمراد الغيب والشهادة بالنسبة لنا وليس للعلم إلا تعلق تنجيزي قديم فقط على التحقيق.
His statement: 'And knowledge' is coordinated with his statement: 'Will', so it is similar to power also in three matters: its relation to possible things, the infinity of its objects, and the necessity of unity for it by consensus of those whose consensus counts. For no one has held that His knowledge is multiple according to the number of known things except Abu Sahl al-Su'luki, who said: [He has] eternal sciences without end. And the impossibility of entering into existence of what has no end does not apply to him because the proof established this impossibility only for the temporal, not for the eternal. And his statement: 'But it encompassed this' means: but knowledge encompassed from the aspect of its relation these possible things which the generality of his statement 'by a possible' indicated, because what is meant is generality as before. The author by this exception removed what would suggest likening knowledge to power in restricting it to possibles as in power and will, but it is not so. Rather it also relates to necessaries and impossibles. And there is no repetition (ita') in his speech due to the different reference of the two demonstrative pronouns, as it is not from the broken meter (mashṭūr al-rajaz) but from its complete meter (tām) as has been mentioned many times. 35 - 'And it also encompassed the necessary and the impossible, and like this is His speech, so let us follow.' And his statement: 'And it also encompassed the necessary and the impossible' means: knowledge included from the aspect of its relation the intellectual necessary (al-wājib al-ʿaqlī) like His essence and attributes, and the intellectual impossible (al-mumtaniʿ al-ʿaqlī) like His partner and taking a son or companion, meaning that He knows the impossibility of that, and He knows that if it existed, such and such corruption would result from it. And 'also' (ayḍan) is a verbal noun from āḍa 'to return', so its meaning is a return to the universality of knowledge. So just as it encompassed possibles, it encompassed necessaries and impossibles. Evidence for the universality of its relation is His saying, exalted: 'And Allah of everything is Knowing' (49:16), and what is meant by 'thing' is absolute matter, not specifically the existent, otherwise it would not match the claim. And His saying, exalted: 'Knower of the unseen and the witnessed' (59:22) means: what is absent from us and what is present to us. So what is meant is the unseen and witnessed relative to us. And knowledge has only one relation: a primordial actualizing relation (taʿalluq tanjīzī qadīm) alone, according to verification.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage explains the nature and scope of divine knowledge (ʿilm). The author begins by noting that knowledge, like power and will, relates to possible things, has infinite objects, and is necessarily one. He then refutes the opinion of Abu Sahl al-Suʿluki, who held that God has multiple eternal sciences corresponding to the number of known things. The author counters that the impossibility of an infinite regress applies only to temporal things, not to the eternal. The main point of the lesson is that knowledge is not restricted to possibles like power and will; it also encompasses the necessary (wājib) and the impossible (mumtaniʿ). This is because knowledge includes understanding of God's essence and attributes (necessary) and the impossibility of a partner or offspring (impossible). The author supports this with two Quranic verses: 'Allah is Knowing of everything' (49:16) – where 'thing' means any entity, not just existent things – and 'Knower of the unseen and the witnessed' (59:22). Finally, he affirms that knowledge has only one type of relation: an eternal actualizing relation (taʿalluq tanjīzī qadīm).

Correction: The passage clarifies that knowledge also includes necessaries (e.g., God's essence) and impossibles (e.g., a partner). The Quranic verse 'Allah is Knowing of everything' uses 'thing' to include non-existents as well.

?
If God's knowledge includes not only what exists but also what is impossible, then your limited understanding is even more humbled. Where do you need to replace your certainty with trust in His perfect knowledge? Make a concrete decision to act on that trust this week.

Intellectual Order Among Eternal Relations
Sanusi explains the intellectual order among eternal relations of power, will, and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conceptual dependency order among the eternal relations of God's knowledge, will, and power, and why there is no temporal order externally.

Core Idea
Knowledge precedes will, and will precedes power in intellectual order, but not in time.

The author of the Jawharah explains that while God's attributes are eternal and have no temporal sequence, there is a conceptual order that reflects dependency. This lesson explores the first part of his analysis, focusing on the eternal relations of power, will, and knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage about eternal relations
Read the first part of the passage that discusses the order among the eternal relations. Pay attention to the terms 'taʿalluq ṣulūḥī' and 'tanjīzī'.
These terms refer to potential and actualizing relations respectively.
2
Identify the three relations and their order
Find the stated intellectual order: knowledge, then will, then power. Notice the dependency: power depends on will, will on knowledge.
This order is only in our understanding, not in external reality.
3
Understand why there is no external order
The passage explains that because these relations are eternal, they cannot have a temporal sequence. If there were an external order, the later would be temporal, contradicting eternity.
Eternal things have no before or after in existence.
4
Reflect on the dependency chain
Consider why knowledge must precede will: knowledge contains the blueprint of what will be willed, and will then directs power to create.
This is a rational necessity, not a temporal one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنَّ تعلقاتِ القدرةِ والإرادة والعلم مترتبة (۱) عند أهل الحق باعتبار التعقل التعلقات القديمة، القديمة، وفي الحقيقة أيضاً في الحادث منها مع القديم، فبين تعلَّقِ القدرة الصلوحي القديم وتعلقِ الإرادة الصلوحي القديم والتنجيزي القديم، وتعلقِ العلم وهو تنجيزي قديم .. ترتيب في التعقل، فنتعقل أولاً تعلَّق العلم، ثم تعلُّق الإرادة، ثم تعلق القدرة، فتعلق القدرة تابع لتعلَّقِ الإرادة، وتعلق الإرادة تابع لتعلقِ العلم، وليس بين هذه التعلقات ترتيب في الخارج لأنها قديمة، والقديم لا ترتيب فيه خارجاً، وإلا لزم أنَّ المتأخر حادث.
وبين تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث وتعلقِ الإرادة التنجيزي القديم والصلوحي القديم وتعلَّقِ العلم وهو تنجيزي قديم كما مر . . ترتيب في الخارج وفي التعقل؛ لأنَّ تعلُّق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث متأخر عن هذه التعلُّقات القديمة ضرورة تأخر الحادث عن القديم . وأما تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادثُ وتعلُّق الإرادة التنجيزي الحادث على القول به.. فبينهما ترتيب في الخارج وفي التعقل، فيكون تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث متأخراً عن تعلق الإرادة التنجيزي الحادثِ على القول به، وقيل: بينهما ترتيب في التعقل فقط ؛ لأنَّه لا يتأخرُ مراد الله عن إرادته. انتهى مُلخصاً مِنْ حاشية العلامة الشَّنواني مع الشرح للشيخ عبد السلام فادع لي ولهم بحسن الختام.
And know that the relations of power, will, and knowledge are ordered (1) according to the people of truth in terms of intellectual consideration: the eternal relations among themselves, and also in actuality regarding the temporal among them with the eternal. So between the primordial potential relation of power (al-taʿalluq al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm li-l-qudra) and the primordial potential relation of will and its primordial actualizing relation, and the relation of knowledge which is a primordial actualizing relation, there is an order in intellection: we intellect first the relation of knowledge, then the relation of will, then the relation of power. So the relation of power is dependent on the relation of will, and the relation of will is dependent on the relation of knowledge. But there is no order among these relations in external reality because they are eternal, and the eternal has no order externally; otherwise the later would be temporal. And between the temporal actualizing relation of power (al-taʿalluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith li-l-qudra) and the primordial actualizing relation of will and its primordial potential relation, and the relation of knowledge which is primordial actualizing as before, there is an order both externally and intellectually, because the temporal actualizing relation of power is subsequent to these eternal relations necessarily due to the temporality of the temporal relative to the eternal. As for the temporal actualizing relation of power and the temporal actualizing relation of will, according to the opinion that holds it, there is an order between them both externally and intellectually: the temporal actualizing relation of power is subsequent to the temporal actualizing relation of will according to that opinion. And it is said: there is an order only intellectually, because God's desired object (murād) is not subsequent to His will. End of summary from the gloss of the scholar al-Shanwānī with the commentary of Shaykh ʿAbd al-Salām; pray for me and them for a good end.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed analysis of the ordering (tartīb) among the relations (taʿalluqāt) of the three attributes: power (qudra), will (irāda), and knowledge (ʿilm). The author distinguishes between two contexts: first, the order among the eternal relations themselves (al-qadīma), which exists only in intellectual consideration (fi'l-taʿaqqul) but not in external reality, because eternal things have no temporal sequence. The intellectual order is: knowledge → will → power, meaning that power depends on will, and will depends on knowledge. Second, when considering the temporal relation of power (al-ḥādith) alongside the eternal relations of will and knowledge, there is an order both intellectually and externally, because the temporal is necessarily later. Third, if one holds that will also has a temporal actualizing relation (on which there is a difference of opinion), then between the temporal power relation and the temporal will relation there is also an external and intellectual order (power after will). However, another opinion says the order is only intellectual, because God's object of will (murād) is not temporally separate from His will. The passage ends with a brief closing supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because God's attributes are eternal, there is no ordering whatsoever among their relations.
Correction: While there is no temporal order, there is a conceptual order of dependency: knowledge precedes will, and will precedes power in the intellect.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the intellectual order of the eternal relations?
A) Power, then will, then knowledge
B) Knowledge, then will, then power
C) Will, then knowledge, then power
D) Knowledge, then power, then will

Key Takeaway
The eternal relations of knowledge, will, and power have an intellectual order of dependency but no temporal sequence.

Temporal Power and Eternal Will and Knowledge
Sanusi explains the order between the temporal power relation and the eternal will and knowledge relations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the temporal actualizing relation of power is ordered after the eternal relations of will and knowledge both intellectually and externally.

Core Idea
The temporal power relation is necessarily later than the eternal relations of will and knowledge.

In the second part of the passage, the author extends the discussion to include the temporal relation of power, explaining that it is ordered after the eternal relations both in intellect and in reality. This lesson covers that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the second Arabic part
Read the section beginning with 'Wa-bayna taʿalluq al-qudra al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith...'. Notice how it contrasts with the previous discussion.
This part introduces the temporal (ḥādith) actualizing relation of power.
2
Note the difference: external order now exists
Unlike the eternal relations among themselves, here the author affirms order both in intellect and in external reality.
The reason is the temporal nature of power's relation.
3
Understand why temporal power must be later
The author says: 'because the temporal actualizing relation of power is subsequent to these eternal relations necessarily due to the temporality of the temporal relative to the eternal.'
Anything temporal comes after the eternal in existence.
4
Connect to the principle
The principle: the temporal (ḥādith) is necessarily later than the eternal (qadīm). This is a basic kalam rule.
This applies to relations of attributes just as to creations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنَّ تعلقاتِ القدرةِ والإرادة والعلم مترتبة (۱) عند أهل الحق باعتبار التعقل التعلقات القديمة، القديمة، وفي الحقيقة أيضاً في الحادث منها مع القديم، فبين تعلَّقِ القدرة الصلوحي القديم وتعلقِ الإرادة الصلوحي القديم والتنجيزي القديم، وتعلقِ العلم وهو تنجيزي قديم .. ترتيب في التعقل، فنتعقل أولاً تعلَّق العلم، ثم تعلُّق الإرادة، ثم تعلق القدرة، فتعلق القدرة تابع لتعلَّقِ الإرادة، وتعلق الإرادة تابع لتعلقِ العلم، وليس بين هذه التعلقات ترتيب في الخارج لأنها قديمة، والقديم لا ترتيب فيه خارجاً، وإلا لزم أنَّ المتأخر حادث.
وبين تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث وتعلقِ الإرادة التنجيزي القديم والصلوحي القديم وتعلَّقِ العلم وهو تنجيزي قديم كما مر . . ترتيب في الخارج وفي التعقل؛ لأنَّ تعلُّق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث متأخر عن هذه التعلُّقات القديمة ضرورة تأخر الحادث عن القديم . وأما تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادثُ وتعلُّق الإرادة التنجيزي الحادث على القول به.. فبينهما ترتيب في الخارج وفي التعقل، فيكون تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث متأخراً عن تعلق الإرادة التنجيزي الحادثِ على القول به، وقيل: بينهما ترتيب في التعقل فقط ؛ لأنَّه لا يتأخرُ مراد الله عن إرادته. انتهى مُلخصاً مِنْ حاشية العلامة الشَّنواني مع الشرح للشيخ عبد السلام فادع لي ولهم بحسن الختام.
And know that the relations of power, will, and knowledge are ordered (1) according to the people of truth in terms of intellectual consideration: the eternal relations among themselves, and also in actuality regarding the temporal among them with the eternal. So between the primordial potential relation of power (al-taʿalluq al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm li-l-qudra) and the primordial potential relation of will and its primordial actualizing relation, and the relation of knowledge which is a primordial actualizing relation, there is an order in intellection: we intellect first the relation of knowledge, then the relation of will, then the relation of power. So the relation of power is dependent on the relation of will, and the relation of will is dependent on the relation of knowledge. But there is no order among these relations in external reality because they are eternal, and the eternal has no order externally; otherwise the later would be temporal. And between the temporal actualizing relation of power (al-taʿalluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith li-l-qudra) and the primordial actualizing relation of will and its primordial potential relation, and the relation of knowledge which is primordial actualizing as before, there is an order both externally and intellectually, because the temporal actualizing relation of power is subsequent to these eternal relations necessarily due to the temporality of the temporal relative to the eternal. As for the temporal actualizing relation of power and the temporal actualizing relation of will, according to the opinion that holds it, there is an order between them both externally and intellectually: the temporal actualizing relation of power is subsequent to the temporal actualizing relation of will according to that opinion. And it is said: there is an order only intellectually, because God's desired object (murād) is not subsequent to His will. End of summary from the gloss of the scholar al-Shanwānī with the commentary of Shaykh ʿAbd al-Salām; pray for me and them for a good end.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed analysis of the ordering (tartīb) among the relations (taʿalluqāt) of the three attributes: power (qudra), will (irāda), and knowledge (ʿilm). The author distinguishes between two contexts: first, the order among the eternal relations themselves (al-qadīma), which exists only in intellectual consideration (fi'l-taʿaqqul) but not in external reality, because eternal things have no temporal sequence. The intellectual order is: knowledge → will → power, meaning that power depends on will, and will depends on knowledge. Second, when considering the temporal relation of power (al-ḥādith) alongside the eternal relations of will and knowledge, there is an order both intellectually and externally, because the temporal is necessarily later. Third, if one holds that will also has a temporal actualizing relation (on which there is a difference of opinion), then between the temporal power relation and the temporal will relation there is also an external and intellectual order (power after will). However, another opinion says the order is only intellectual, because God's object of will (murād) is not temporally separate from His will. The passage ends with a brief closing supplication.
