Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is there an external order between the temporal power relation and the eternal will/knowledge relations?
A) Because the eternal relations are also temporal
B) Because the temporal is necessarily later than the eternal
C) Because power is always the last stage
D) Because the author follows a particular school

Key Takeaway
The temporal relation of power is necessarily later than the eternal relations of will and knowledge, both conceptually and temporally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does knowing that every temporal event in your life, including your own choices, is preceded by God's eternal will and knowledge affect the way you make decisions? Are you living in humble submission to His eternal decree?
?
The lesson says the temporal power relation is later than the eternal will. When you pray, do you truly believe that your prayer is temporally placed after God's eternal will? How does that shape your reliance on Him rather than on your own efforts?
?
If the temporal is necessarily later than the eternal, what does that imply about your own merits and actions? Can anything you do truly precede God's will? How does that humble you, and what specific act of trust can you commit to today because of this truth?

Temporal Power and Temporal Will: Two Opinions
Sanusi presents two opinions on the ordering of temporal power and temporal will relations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly opinions on whether there is an external order between the temporal relations of power and will.

Core Idea
Scholars disagree whether temporal power is later than temporal will in time or only intellectually.

The author concludes with a discussion of a point of disagreement: if we accept that will also has a temporal relation, does it have an external order with temporal power? Two views are presented, and this lesson unpacks them.

Guided Path
1
Read the final Arabic part
Read the section starting with 'Wa-ammā taʿalluq al-qudra al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith...' until the end of the passage.
This part is about the order between temporal power and temporal will.
2
Identify the two opinions
First opinion: there is an order both externally and intellectually (temporal power after temporal will). Second opinion: order only intellectually.
The second opinion is introduced with 'wa-qīla'.
3
Understand the reasoning for each
First opinion: because power executes what will desires, so in reality power's act comes after will's act. Second opinion: because the object of will (the thing willed) is not temporally after the will itself; they occur simultaneously, so no external priority.
The second opinion is based on the fact that God's will and its object are not separate in time.
4
Note the connection to the principle
The second opinion argues that 'God's desired object (murād) is not subsequent to His will.' This is a key theological point.
This prevents any temporal lag between God's will and its fulfillment.

Misconception & Correction

?

?

?

How does this truth confront your own tendency to delay obedience after deciding to act? Identify one area where you procrastinate in obeying God, and set a specific time today to act on your will.

The Meaning of 'Shay' and the Attachment of Knowledge
Defines 'shay' and states knowledge's attachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what is meant by 'shay' in the verse and why God's knowledge has only an eternal actualizing attachment.

Core Idea
Divine knowledge attaches to all matters, whether existent or not, through a single eternal mode.

In this passage, Sanusi clarifies the term 'shay' (thing) in the verse {Knower of the unseen and the witnessed}. He argues that it means absolute matter, not merely the existent, to affirm that God knows everything. This leads to the conclusion that knowledge has only one type of attachment: an eternal actualizing attachment.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of shay'
Read the Arabic and translation for the definition of shay' as 'absolute matter'. Notice the reason given: otherwise it would not match the claim.
This prevents limiting God's knowledge to only existent things.
2
Analyse the verse citation
Examine how the verse is interpreted to mean the unseen and witnessed relative to us. This supports the broader definition.
3
Identify the attachment of knowledge
Find the statement about knowledge having only an eternal actualizing attachment. Understand what 'tanzīzī' and 'qadīm' mean here.
This is the key conclusion.
4
Reflect on why this matters
Consider why defining shay' broadly is necessary for the doctrine of God's omniscience.
It avoids restricting knowledge to only what exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُرَادُ بِالشَّيْءِ: مطلق الأمر، لا خصوص الموجود، وإلا لم يطابق المُدعى، وقوله تعالى: ﴿عَلِمُ الْغَيْبِ وَالشَّهَادَة) [الحشر: ۲۲]؛ أي: ما غاب عنا وما حضر لنا، فالمراد الغيب والشهادة بالنسبة لنا وليس للعلم إلا تعلق تنجيزي قديم فقط على التحقيق. واعلم أنَّ تعلقاتِ القدرةِ والإرادة والعلم مترتبة عند أهل الحق باعتبار التعقل التعلقات القديمة، القديمة، وفي الحقيقة أيضاً في الحادث منها مع القديم، فبين تعلَّقِ القدرة الصلوحي القديم وتعلقِ الإرادة الصلوحي القديم والتنجيزي القديم، وتعلقِ العلم وهو تنجيزي قديم .. ترتيب في التعقل، فنتعقل أولاً تعلَّق العلم، ثم تعلُّق الإرادة، ثم تعلق القدرة، فتعلق القدرة تابع لتعلَّقِ الإرادة، وتعلق الإرادة تابع لتعلقِ العلم، وليس بين هذه التعلقات ترتيب في الخارج لأنها قديمة، والقديم لا ترتيب فيه خارجاً، وإلا لزم أنَّ المتأخر حادث. وبين تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث وتعلقِ الإرادة التنجيزي القديم والصلوحي القديم وتعلَّقِ العلم وهو تنجيزي قديم كما مر . . ترتيب في الخارج وفي التعقل؛ لأنَّ تعلُّق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث متأخر عن هذه التعلُّقات القديمة ضرورة تأخر الحادث عن القديم . وأما تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادثُ وتعلُّق الإرادة التنجيزي الحادث على القول به.. فبينهما ترتيب في الخارج وفي التعقل، فيكون تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث متأخراً عن تعلق الإرادة التنجيزي الحادثِ على القول به، وقيل: بينهما ترتيب في التعقل فقط ؛ لأنَّه لا يتأخرُ مراد الله عن إرادته. انتهى مُلخصاً مِنْ حاشية العلامة الشَّنواني مع الشرح للشيخ عبد السلام فادع لي ولهم بحسن الختام.
And what is meant by 'shay'' [thing] is: absolute matter, not specifically the existent, otherwise it would not match the claim. And His saying, Exalted is He, {Knower of the unseen and the witnessed} [al-Hashr 22] means: what is hidden from us and what is present to us. So what is meant is the unseen and the witnessed relative to us, and knowledge has only an eternal actualizing attachment alone upon verification. And know that the attachments of power, will, and knowledge are ordered according to the people of truth in consideration of intellection of the eternal attachments, and also in reality regarding the temporal ones with the eternal. So between the eternal possibility attachment of power and the eternal possibility and actualizing attachment of will, and the attachment of knowledge which is an eternal actualizing attachment, there is an ordering in intellection: we first intellect the attachment of knowledge, then the attachment of will, then the attachment of power. So the attachment of power follows the attachment of will, and the attachment of will follows the attachment of knowledge. And there is no ordering externally among these attachments because they are eternal, and the eternal has no ordering externally; otherwise it would necessitate that the later is temporal. And between the temporal actualizing attachment of power and the eternal actualizing and possibility attachment of will and the attachment of knowledge which is eternal actualizing as mentioned, there is an ordering externally and in intellection, because the temporal actualizing attachment of power is posterior to these eternal attachments, necessarily due to the posteriority of the temporal to the eternal. As for the temporal actualizing attachment of power and the temporal actualizing attachment of will according to the statement thereof, there is between them an ordering externally and in intellection; so the temporal actualizing attachment of power is posterior to the temporal actualizing attachment of will according to the statement thereof. And it is said: between them there is only an ordering in intellection, because the willed of God is not posterior to His will. It ends, summarized from the gloss of the scholar al-Shanwānī with the commentary of Shaykh ʿAbd al-Salām; pray for me and for them for a good end.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage discusses the ordering of the attachments (taʿalluqāt) of the divine attributes of knowledge (ʿilm), will (irāda), and power (qudra). It begins by clarifying what is meant by 'shay'' (thing) in the verse: it is absolute matter (muṭlaq al-amr), not specifically the existent, to match the claim that God knows everything. Then it explains that God's knowledge has only one attachment: an eternal actualizing attachment (taʿalluq tanzīzī qadīm). The main argument: The attachments of power, will, and knowledge are ordered in the mind (taʿaqqul) when considering the eternal attachments, and also in reality for the temporal ones relative to the eternal. For the eternal attachments, the order is: first knowledge, then will, then power. This order exists only in the mind, not externally, because eternal things have no temporal sequence; otherwise the later would be temporal (ḥādith). For the temporal actualizing attachment of power compared to the eternal attachments of will and knowledge, there is ordering both externally and mentally, because the temporal is necessarily posterior to the eternal. Finally, between two temporal attachments (power and will according to a view), there is ordering both externally and mentally, but some say only mentally because God's will does not delay what He wills. The passage ends with a note that it is summarized from the gloss of al-Shanwānī.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'shay'' refers only to existent things.
Correction: The text clarifies it means absolute matter, including the non-existent.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is 'shay'' defined as 'absolute matter' rather than 'the existent'?
A) Because the existent is too limited.
B) To match the claim that God's knowledge encompasses all things, including the non-existent.
C) Because the verse uses the word 'al-shay''.
D) Because it is a philosophical term.

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge encompasses all matters, both existent and non-existent, through a single eternal actualizing attachment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After learning that God's knowledge includes every hidden thought and future sin, what specific step will you take in the next 24 hours to bring one area of your inner life into alignment with your outward worship?
?
If you truly believe that God's knowledge is eternal and actualizing—meaning He knows your repentance before you repent—how should that affect your urgency in turning back to Him today? What is one thing you have been delaying that you can commit to right now?

The Ordering of Attachments of Power, Will, and Knowledge
Orders the attachments of power, will, and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical ordering of the attachments of power, will, and knowledge, both in the mind and in external reality.

Core Idea
Eternal attachments are ordered only in the mind; temporal attachments follow eternal ones in both mind and time.

Having established the attachment of knowledge, the text now examines how the attachments of power, will, and knowledge are ordered. The author distinguishes between ordering in the mind (bi-iʿtibār al-taʿaqqul) and ordering in external reality (fī al-khārij). For the eternal attachments, only mental ordering exists; for temporal attachments relative to eternal, ordering is both mental and external.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ordering
Read the text to find where it discusses ordering in intellection (taʿaqqul) and ordering externally. Notice that these are distinct.
2
Understand the order among eternal attachments
The text states: knowledge first, then will, then power. But this order is only in the mind, not externally, because eternal things have no temporal sequence.
If there were an external order, the later would be temporal.
3
Examine the order between temporal power and eternal attachments
The temporal actualizing attachment of power is posterior to the eternal attachments of will and knowledge in both mind and external reality, because temporal is necessarily after eternal.
4
Consider the controversy about two temporal attachments
According to one view, the temporal attachment of power is posterior to the temporal attachment of will in both mind and time. Another view says only in mind, because God's will does not delay its object.
This shows the nuance in kalam argumentation.

وَالْمُرَادُ بِالشَّيْءِ: مطلق الأمر، لا خصوص الموجود، وإلا لم يطابق المُدعى، وقوله تعالى: ﴿عَلِمُ الْغَيْبِ وَالشَّهَادَة) [الحشر: ۲۲]؛ أي: ما غاب عنا وما حضر لنا، فالمراد الغيب والشهادة بالنسبة لنا وليس للعلم إلا تعلق تنجيزي قديم فقط على التحقيق. واعلم أنَّ تعلقاتِ القدرةِ والإرادة والعلم مترتبة عند أهل الحق باعتبار التعقل التعلقات القديمة، القديمة، وفي الحقيقة أيضاً في الحادث منها مع القديم، فبين تعلَّقِ القدرة الصلوحي القديم وتعلقِ الإرادة الصلوحي القديم والتنجيزي القديم، وتعلقِ العلم وهو تنجيزي قديم .. ترتيب في التعقل، فنتعقل أولاً تعلَّق العلم، ثم تعلُّق الإرادة، ثم تعلق القدرة، فتعلق القدرة تابع لتعلَّقِ الإرادة، وتعلق الإرادة تابع لتعلقِ العلم، وليس بين هذه التعلقات ترتيب في الخارج لأنها قديمة، والقديم لا ترتيب فيه خارجاً، وإلا لزم أنَّ المتأخر حادث. وبين تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث وتعلقِ الإرادة التنجيزي القديم والصلوحي القديم وتعلَّقِ العلم وهو تنجيزي قديم كما مر . . ترتيب في الخارج وفي التعقل؛ لأنَّ تعلُّق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث متأخر عن هذه التعلُّقات القديمة ضرورة تأخر الحادث عن القديم . وأما تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادثُ وتعلُّق الإرادة التنجيزي الحادث على القول به.. فبينهما ترتيب في الخارج وفي التعقل، فيكون تعلق القدرة التنجيزي الحادث متأخراً عن تعلق الإرادة التنجيزي الحادثِ على القول به، وقيل: بينهما ترتيب في التعقل فقط ؛ لأنَّه لا يتأخرُ مراد الله عن إرادته. انتهى مُلخصاً مِنْ حاشية العلامة الشَّنواني مع الشرح للشيخ عبد السلام فادع لي ولهم بحسن الختام.
And what is meant by 'shay'' [thing] is: absolute matter, not specifically the existent, otherwise it would not match the claim. And His saying, Exalted is He, {Knower of the unseen and the witnessed} [al-Hashr 22] means: what is hidden from us and what is present to us. So what is meant is the unseen and the witnessed relative to us, and knowledge has only an eternal actualizing attachment alone upon verification. And know that the attachments of power, will, and knowledge are ordered according to the people of truth in consideration of intellection of the eternal attachments, and also in reality regarding the temporal ones with the eternal. So between the eternal possibility attachment of power and the eternal possibility and actualizing attachment of will, and the attachment of knowledge which is an eternal actualizing attachment, there is an ordering in intellection: we first intellect the attachment of knowledge, then the attachment of will, then the attachment of power. So the attachment of power follows the attachment of will, and the attachment of will follows the attachment of knowledge. And there is no ordering externally among these attachments because they are eternal, and the eternal has no ordering externally; otherwise it would necessitate that the later is temporal. And between the temporal actualizing attachment of power and the eternal actualizing and possibility attachment of will and the attachment of knowledge which is eternal actualizing as mentioned, there is an ordering externally and in intellection, because the temporal actualizing attachment of power is posterior to these eternal attachments, necessarily due to the posteriority of the temporal to the eternal. As for the temporal actualizing attachment of power and the temporal actualizing attachment of will according to the statement thereof, there is between them an ordering externally and in intellection; so the temporal actualizing attachment of power is posterior to the temporal actualizing attachment of will according to the statement thereof. And it is said: between them there is only an ordering in intellection, because the willed of God is not posterior to His will. It ends, summarized from the gloss of the scholar al-Shanwānī with the commentary of Shaykh ʿAbd al-Salām; pray for me and for them for a good end.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage discusses the ordering of the attachments (taʿalluqāt) of the divine attributes of knowledge (ʿilm), will (irāda), and power (qudra). It begins by clarifying what is meant by 'shay'' (thing) in the verse: it is absolute matter (muṭlaq al-amr), not specifically the existent, to match the claim that God knows everything. Then it explains that God's knowledge has only one attachment: an eternal actualizing attachment (taʿalluq tanzīzī qadīm). The main argument: The attachments of power, will, and knowledge are ordered in the mind (taʿaqqul) when considering the eternal attachments, and also in reality for the temporal ones relative to the eternal. For the eternal attachments, the order is: first knowledge, then will, then power. This order exists only in the mind, not externally, because eternal things have no temporal sequence; otherwise the later would be temporal (ḥādith). For the temporal actualizing attachment of power compared to the eternal attachments of will and knowledge, there is ordering both externally and mentally, because the temporal is necessarily posterior to the eternal. Finally, between two temporal attachments (power and will according to a view), there is ordering both externally and mentally, but some say only mentally because God's will does not delay what He wills. The passage ends with a note that it is summarized from the gloss of al-Shanwānī.

صلوحي
قديم
حادث

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the eternal attachments of God's attributes are ordered temporally.
Correction: The text explicitly states there is no external ordering among eternal attachments, because the eternal has no temporal sequence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is there no external ordering among the eternal attachments of knowledge, will, and power?
A) Because they are identical.
B) Because the eternal has no temporal sequence; otherwise the later would be temporal.
C) Because only the temporal attachments have order.
D) Because the order is only in the mind.

Key Takeaway
The attachments of God's attributes are ordered intellectually but not temporally for the eternal ones; temporal attachments follow the eternal ones in both mind and time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just studied that God's knowledge, will, and power are eternally simultaneous, even though we understand them in a sequence. Do you live your life as if God's knowledge of your sins already includes His will and power to forgive or punish? How does this reality affect the urgency of your repentance right now, not later?
?
If the eternal attachments are ordered only in our minds, then God's will for your life is not waiting on His knowledge or power—they are one eternal act. When you face a decision, do you trust that God's will for you is already perfectly aligned with His knowledge of your situation, or do you assume God needs to 'catch up' with your choices? How can you surrender more to His simultaneous decree?
?
This lesson teaches that temporal attachments follow eternal ones in both mind and time. Consider one specific area where you desire God's power to act in your life (e.g., guidance, provision). Are you more focused on the temporal outcome (God's power creating it) or on the eternal reality of His will and knowledge that already precede it? How can you shift your focus to exalt God's eternal attributes rather than just awaiting His temporal action?

God's Speech Resembles His Knowledge in Three Rulings
States that God's speech shares three rulings with His knowledge, with a distinction in attachment mode.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's eternal speech is like His knowledge in terms of generality, infiniteness, and oneness, and how their modes of attachment differ.

Core Idea
God's speech is one, all-encompassing, and infinite, just like His knowledge.

This passage from the commentary on al-Jawhara explains a key point about God's attribute of speech. Just as God's knowledge encompasses all things, His eternal speech similarly applies to the necessary, possible, and impossible. However, the way speech relates to objects is different from knowledge: speech indicates, while knowledge discloses. Let's explore these three rulings and the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings of similarity
Read the passage to find the three ways in which God's speech is like His knowledge: generality of attachment, non-finiteness of objects, and oneness.
Each ruling is explicitly mentioned after 'الأحكام الثلاثة'.
2
Understand the argument for non-finiteness
Notice the reasoning: if speech were limited to finite objects, that would be an arbitrary preference without a reason (tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ), which is impossible for God.
The example of Paradise's ever-renewing bliss illustrates infinity.
3
Distinguish attachment types
Knowledge attaches by disclosure (inkishāfī), meaning it uncovers the object. Speech attaches by indication (dalāla), meaning it points to the object without revealing its essence.
This difference does not affect the three shared rulings.
4
Note the two modes of speech's attachment
For matters other than command/prohibition, speech has an eternal actualizing attachment. For commands/prohibitions, it has an eternal possibility attachment before the act and a temporal actualizing attachment after.
This shows the subtlety of the topic, as the author warns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَمِثلُ ذَا كَلامُهُ) أي : ومثل علمه تعالى كلامه، قاسم الإشارة عائد على العلم، و(مثل) خبر مقدمٌ ، و(كلامه) مبتدأ مؤخر ، والتقدير : وكلامه النفسي القديم القائم بذاته تعالى مثل العلم في الأحكام الثلاثة : وهي عموم تعلقه بالواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات وعدم تناهي متعلقاته، وإيجاب وحدته، فعموم تعلقه لصلوحه للجميع . وعدم تناهي متعلقاته لا متناع التخصيص بشيء يتناهى ؛ لأنه ترجيح بلا مرجح، ومن متعلقاته نعيم الجنان وهو لا يتناهى بل يتجدد شيئاً فشيئاً وهكذا . وإيجاب وحدته ؛ لأنَّه لم يردِ السمع بالتعدد، بل العقد الإجماع على نفي كلام ثان قديم والمثليَّةُ إنما هي في الثلاثة الأحكام المذكورة وإن اختلفت جهة التعلق ؛ لأنَّ تعلَّق العلم تعلق انكشافي، وتعلق الكلام تعلق دلالة. وهو تعلق تنجيزي قديم بالنظر لغير الأمر والنهي، فهو يدلُّ أزلاً على أنَّ ذاته وصفاته تعالى واجبةٌ وأنَّ الشريك والصاحبة والولد مستحيلة، وأن ولد زيد ورزقه وعلمه جائزة، ويدلُّ أزلاً أيضاً على أنَّ من أطاع فله الجنَّةُ، ومن عصى فله النار، والأول وعد، والثاني وعيد وهكذا، وأما بالنظر للأمر والنهي فعلى اشتراط وجود المأمور والمنهي يكون له تعلق صلوحي قديم قبل وجود المأمور والمنهي، وتنجيزي حادث بعده كما تقدم تحقيقه. قوله : (فَلْنَتَّبِعْ) بالنون أو بالتاء أوله ، وفيه إشارة إلى غموض المحل وصعوبته، فيشير لى أنه ليس لنا في هذا المقام إلا اتباع القوم، خصوصاً في إثبات التعلقاتِ الأزليَّة.
His saying: 'And such is His speech' means: And His speech, exalted be He, is like His knowledge. The demonstrative pronoun refers back to knowledge, and 'like' is a predicate forward, and 'His speech' is a subject delayed, so the estimation is: And His internal eternal speech subsisting in His essence, exalted be He, is like knowledge in three rulings: they are the generality of its attachment to the necessary, possible, and impossible things; the non-finiteness of its objects; and the affirmation of its oneness. So the generality of its attachment is due to its suitability for all. And the non-finiteness of its objects is due to the impossibility of specifying [with] something finite, because that would be a preference without a preferrer. And among its objects is the bliss of Paradise, and it is non-finite, rather it is renewed little by little, and so on. And the affirmation of its oneness is because revelation did not indicate multiplicity, rather the consensus has settled on negating a second eternal speech. And the likeness is only in the three mentioned rulings, although the aspect of attachment differs; because the attachment of knowledge is an attachment of disclosure, and the attachment of speech is an attachment of indication. And it is an eternal actualizing attachment with regard to other than command and prohibition. So it indicates eternally that His essence and attributes, exalted be He, are necessary, and that the partner, consort, and child are impossible, and that Zayd's son, his provision, and his knowledge are possible. And it indicates eternally also that whoever obeys will have Paradise, and whoever disobeys will have Hellfire; the first is a promise, the second is a threat, and so on. And with regard to command and prohibition, upon the condition of the existence of the commanded and the prohibited, it has an eternal possibility attachment before the existence of the commanded and the prohibited, and a temporal actualizing attachment after it, as its verification has preceded. His saying: 'So let us follow' with a nun or with a ta at its beginning, and in it is an indication of the obscurity of the place and its difficulty, so he indicates that we have in this position nothing but following the folk, especially in proving the eternal attachments.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line 'And such is His speech' from the poem. It explains that God's eternal internal speech (al-kalām al-nafsī al-qadīm) is like His knowledge in three rulings: (1) general attachment to all categories: the necessary (wājibāt), possible (jāʾizāt), and impossible (mustaḥīlāt); (2) infinite objects of attachment; (3) necessary oneness. The generality is because speech is suitable for all objects. The infiniteness of objects is argued: if it were limited to finite things, that would be a preference without a preferrer (tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ), which is invalid; an example of infinite objects is the ever-renewing bliss of Paradise. The oneness is because revelation does not indicate multiple eternal speeches, and consensus negates a second eternal speech. The likeness is only in these three aspects; they differ in the mode of attachment: knowledge attaches by disclosure (inkishāfī), speech by indication (dalāla). The attachment of speech is eternal actualizing concerning matters other than command and prohibition; it indicates eternally that God's essence and attributes are necessary, that a partner or offspring is impossible, and that contingent things like Zayd's son or provision are possible. It also indicates the consequences of obedience and disobedience. For command and prohibition, speech has an eternal possibility attachment (taʿalluq ṣalūḥī qadīm) prior to the existence of the commanded/prohibited, and a temporal actualizing attachment after their existence. The passage ends with commentary on the line 'So let us follow', indicating that this topic is difficult and one must follow the authorities, especially in proving eternal attachments.

وعيد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think God's speech is multiple like human speech, or that it is limited in scope.
Correction: The text establishes that God's speech is one, all-encompassing, and infinite, just like His knowledge, though the mode of attachment differs.

Checkpoint
What is the main difference between the attachment of knowledge and the attachment of speech according to the passage?
A) Knowledge attaches to possible things only; speech to necessary things.
B) Knowledge attaches by disclosure; speech attaches by indication.
C) Knowledge is eternal; speech is temporal.
D) Knowledge is one; speech is multiple.

Key Takeaway
God's eternal speech shares with His knowledge the properties of generality, infinity, and unity, but differs in that speech indicates objects while knowledge discloses them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
God's speech eternally indicates that whoever obeys will have Paradise and whoever disobeys will have Hellfire. Is your daily life driven by the reality of this eternal verdict, or do you live as if the consequences are distant or uncertain? What one habit would change if you truly believed that God's speech has already decreed the outcome of your actions?
?
The author calls this topic obscure and says we must follow the authorities. In what areas of your faith do you rely on your own reasoning rather than submitting to the scholars? Are there doctrines you find uncomfortable and try to reinterpret? Pray about one such issue and commit to seeking guidance from reliable sources.
?
God's speech is one, yet it commands and prohibits based on conditions. Is there a command of God that you know applies to you now but you delay obeying, thinking it only applies in some future situation? What is holding you back from immediate obedience?

Hearing and Sight Attach to Every Existing Thing
Explanation of the verse stating hearing and sight apply to all existents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the poet and commentator assert that the divine attributes of hearing and sight are not limited but attach to every existent.

Core Idea
Hearing and sight of Allah encompass all existence.

This lesson examines a line from the Jawharat al-Tawhid that expands the scope of divine hearing and sight. The text clarifies that these attributes are not restricted to specific types of objects but can be attached to every existing thing. Understanding this helps us appreciate the comprehensiveness of Allah's perception.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic line and explanation
Begin by reading the verse (line 36) and the commentary that follows. Note how the commentator unpacks the meaning.
The verse is short, but the commentary provides grammatical details.
2
Identify the grammatical structure
Focus on how 'kullu mawjūdin' is parsed. The commentator gives two possible grammatical analyses. Understand each parsing.
The different parsings do not change the core meaning.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Ask yourself: What does it mean that hearing and sight attach to every existent? How does this affect our understanding of these divine attributes?
This connects to the attribute of pervasiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٦ - وَكُلُّ مَوْجُودٍ أَيْظُ لِلسَّمْعِ بِهْ كَذَا البَصَرْ إِدْرَاكُهُ إِنْ قِيلَ بِهْ قوله : (وَكُلُّ مَوْجُودٍ أَيْظُ لِلسَّمْع بِه) أي : وكل موجود علق للسمع به، فأنط : فعل به، أمر من الإناطة؛ وهي التعليق وكلُّ : مبتدأ خبره جملة (أنط للسمع به)، أو مفعول لمحذوف يفسِّرُهُ المذكور من باب الاشتغال؛ على حد زيداً مرَّ به، والتقدير : اقصد
36. And every existent also is attached to hearing, likewise the sight: its perception if one holds it. His saying: 'And every existent also is attached to hearing' means: And every existent is attached to hearing. 'Fa-anit' is a verb in the imperative from 'ināṭa' which is to attach. 'Kullu' is a subject, its predicate is the sentence 'anit li l-samʿi bihi', or it is a direct object of an omitted verb that is explained by the mentioned one on the pattern of 'Zaydan marra bihi', and the estimation is: intend.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is the explanation of a new verse of the poem (number 36) and its commentary. The poem states: 'And every existent also is attached to hearing, likewise the sight: its perception if one holds that.' The commentator explains that 'every existent is attached to hearing' means that hearing can be attached to any existent. The verb 'anit' is a command form meaning 'attach', derived from 'ināṭa'. The grammatical structure: 'kullu' is the subject, and the sentence 'anit li l-samʿi bihi' is its predicate. Alternatively, it can be parsed as an object of an omitted verb on the pattern of 'Zaydan marra bihi' (like 'Zayd, he passed by him'), meaning 'intend every existent and attach it to hearing'. The commentary also mentions that the same applies to sight: its perception of every existent if one holds that sight can perceive everything. This passage asserts the potential generality of hearing and sight as divine attributes.

Key Terms
السمع
البصر
الإدراك
الإناطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Hearing and sight only perceive sounds and sights respectively, not all existence.
Correction: The text states that hearing and sight can attach to every existent, indicating their scope is universal.

Checkpoint

A) Hearing only attaches to living things.
B) Hearing can be attached to every existent.
C) Hearing is limited to sound.
D) Hearing only exists in humans.

Key Takeaway
The divine attributes of hearing and sight are all-encompassing, attaching to every existing thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Universal and Infinite Scope of Divine Attributes
Sanusi defines the universality and infinity of divine attributes' relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine attributes relate universally to all rational categories and cannot be limited to finite things.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are not limited; they relate to everything necessary, possible, and impossible.

Sanusi begins by asserting that divine attributes, particularly knowledge and speech, have a universal relation to all rational judgments. This universality is not arbitrary; it follows from God's perfection. In this passage, he explains why the relation cannot be finite and provides an example of infinite relata: the bliss of Paradise.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once slowly, then compare with the translation. Notice the key terms: عموم التعلق, الواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات, عدم تناهي.
2
Understand the three categories
Identify the three categories: necessary (واجبات), possible (جائزات), impossible (مستحيلات). Why must the attribute relate to all three?
This is foundational for Islamic theology.
3
Grasp the argument for non-finiteness
The passage argues that limiting the attribute to a finite set would require a preferrer without reason. See if you can follow this logical deduction.
Example: bliss of Paradise is infinite and renewed.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why is it important that divine attributes are not limited? How does this affect our understanding of God?
This is part of tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي عموم تعلقه بالواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات وعدم تناهي متعلقاته، وإيجاب وحدته، فعموم تعلقه لصلوحه للجميع. وعدم تناهي متعلقاته لامتناع التخصيص بشيء يتناهى؛ لأنه ترجيح بلا مرجح. ومن متعلقاته نعيم الجنان وهو لا يتناهى بل يتجدد شيئاً فشيئاً وهكذا. وإيجاب وحدته؛ لأنَّه لم يرد السمع بالتعدد، بل انعقد الإجماع على نفي كلام ثان قديم والمثلية إنما هي في الثلاثة الأحكام المذكورة وإن اختلفت جهة التعلق؛ لأنَّ تعلق العلم تعلق انكشافي، وتعلق الكلام تعلق دلالة. وهو تعلق تنجيزي قديم بالنظر لغير الأمر والنهي، فهو يدل أزلاً على أنَّ ذاته وصفاته تعالى واجبة، وعلى أنَّ الشريك والصاحبة والولد مستحيلة، وأن ولد زيد ورزقه وعلمه جائزة، ويدل أزلاً أيضاً على أنَّ من أطاع فله الجنة، ومن عصى فله النار، والأول وعد، والثاني وعيد وهكذا، وأما بالنظر للأمر والنهي فعلى اشتراط وجود المأمور والمنهي يكون له تعلق صلوحي قديم قبل وجود المأمور والمنهي، وتنجيزي حادث بعده كما تقدم تحقيقه
And it is the universality of its relation to the necessary, possible, and impossible things, and the non-finiteness of its relata, and the necessitation of its oneness. So the universality of its relation is due to its suitability for all. And the non-finiteness of its relata is due to the impossibility of specifying it with something finite; because that would be a preferment without a preferrer. And among its relata is the bliss of Paradise, which is not finite but is renewed little by little, and so on. And the necessitation of its oneness is because revelation did not indicate multiplicity; rather consensus has been reached on negating a second eternal speech, and similarity is only in the three mentioned judgments even if the aspect of relation differs. Because the relation of knowledge is a relation of unveiling (inkishafi), and the relation of speech is a relation of indication (dalala). It (speech) is an eternal determinate relation (taluq tanjizi qadim) with respect to other than command and prohibition. So it indicates eternally that His essence and His exalted attributes are necessary, and that the partner, consort, and child are impossible, and that the son of Zayd, his provision, and his knowledge are possible. And it indicates eternally also that whoever obeys will have Paradise, and whoever disobeys will have Hellfire; the first is a promise, the second is a threat, and so on. And as for with respect to command and prohibition, subject to the condition of the existence of the commanded and the prohibited, it has an eternal potential relation (taluq salahi qadim) before the existence of the commanded and the prohibited, and a temporal determinate relation (taluq tanjizi hadith) after it, as its verification has preceded.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the universality and oneness of certain divine attributes, specifically knowledge and speech. It begins by stating that the attribute in question has a universal relation to all three categories of rational judgments: necessary (wajibat), possible (ja'izat), and impossible (mustahilat). This universality cannot be limited; any limitation would be arbitrary without a reason (tarjih bila murajjih). An example of an infinite relatum is the bliss of Paradise, which is continually renewed. The passage then argues for the oneness of the attribute (here, speech) because revelation does not indicate multiple eternal speeches and there is consensus against a second eternal speech. The similarity of attributes is only in the three judgments, though the aspect of relation differs. The passage distinguishes between knowledge and speech: the relation of knowledge is one of unveiling (inkishafi) – the thing is disclosed to God – while the relation of speech is one of indication (dalala) – the speech indicates the reality of things. It explains that speech has an eternal determinate relation regarding matters not involving commands or prohibitions; for example, it indicates eternally that God's essence and attributes are necessary, that a partner is impossible, and that Zayd's son is possible. For command and prohibition, there is an eternal potential relation before the commanded/subject exists, and a temporal determinate relation after. This is the commentator's resolution to the issue of taluq.

Key Terms
عموم التعلق
الواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات
عدم تناهي
ترجيح بلا مرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine attributes only relate to certain things or are finite.
Correction: They relate universally to all rational categories and have infinite relata.

Checkpoint
What would it imply if the relation of a divine attribute were limited to a finite set of things?
A) It would be impossible.
B) It would require an arbitrary preference.
C) It would still be acceptable.
D) It would prove God's power.

Key Takeaway
Divine attributes are universal and infinite in their relation; any limitation would be logically arbitrary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe that Allah’s attributes relate to everything, including your deepest secrets and future sins. Do you live as if that is true? Or do you secretly assume some things are hidden from His knowledge? What would change in your life if you fully internalized that nothing escapes His universal relation?
?
The bliss of Paradise is described as endlessly renewed. Does your hope for the afterlife go beyond simply 'entering Paradise' to craving that infinite renewal? Or have you settled for a static image of Paradise that doesn't match the dynamic, infinite relata mentioned here?
?
If any limitation on God’s attributes is arbitrary (tarjih bila murajjih), then your own limited conception of God—perhaps shaped by culture or comfort—is not just incomplete but logically indefensible. Are you willing to tear down your own mental restrictions and worship the infinite God as He truly is, even if it unsettles you?

The Oneness of Divine Speech and Its Twofold Relation
Sanusi argues for the oneness of divine speech and explains its two modes of relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine speech is one and eternal, and how it relates to things through two modes: determinate and potential.

Core Idea
Divine speech is one, eternal, and relates to all things either determinately or potentially.

Having established the universality of divine attributes, Sanusi now focuses on speech. He argues for the oneness of speech based on revelation and consensus, and distinguishes between the relation of knowledge (unveiling) and speech (indication). He then elaborates on the two types of relation for speech: an eternal determinate relation for non-commands, and a potential relation before commands exist.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text for this lesson, noting terms like تعلق انكشافي, تعلق دلالة, تعلق تنجيزي, تعلق صلوحي.
2
Understand the proof for oneness
The passage says revelation did not indicate multiplicity, and there is consensus against a second eternal speech. Why is this important?
This guards against polytheism or belief in multiple divine speeches.
3
Distinguish knowledge and speech
Knowledge's relation is unveiling (the thing is disclosed), speech's relation is indication (the speech points to the thing). Contrast these.
This affects how we understand divine attributes.
4
Grasp the two relations of speech
For matters other than command/prohibition, speech has an eternal determinate relation. For commands/prohibitions, it has a potential relation (before the commanded exists) and a temporal determinate relation (after).
Example: God's command 'Pray' relates potentially before humans exist.

وهي عموم تعلقه بالواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات وعدم تناهي متعلقاته، وإيجاب وحدته، فعموم تعلقه لصلوحه للجميع. وعدم تناهي متعلقاته لامتناع التخصيص بشيء يتناهى؛ لأنه ترجيح بلا مرجح. ومن متعلقاته نعيم الجنان وهو لا يتناهى بل يتجدد شيئاً فشيئاً وهكذا. وإيجاب وحدته؛ لأنَّه لم يرد السمع بالتعدد، بل انعقد الإجماع على نفي كلام ثان قديم والمثلية إنما هي في الثلاثة الأحكام المذكورة وإن اختلفت جهة التعلق؛ لأنَّ تعلق العلم تعلق انكشافي، وتعلق الكلام تعلق دلالة. وهو تعلق تنجيزي قديم بالنظر لغير الأمر والنهي، فهو يدل أزلاً على أنَّ ذاته وصفاته تعالى واجبة، وعلى أنَّ الشريك والصاحبة والولد مستحيلة، وأن ولد زيد ورزقه وعلمه جائزة، ويدل أزلاً أيضاً على أنَّ من أطاع فله الجنة، ومن عصى فله النار، والأول وعد، والثاني وعيد وهكذا، وأما بالنظر للأمر والنهي فعلى اشتراط وجود المأمور والمنهي يكون له تعلق صلوحي قديم قبل وجود المأمور والمنهي، وتنجيزي حادث بعده كما تقدم تحقيقه
And it is the universality of its relation to the necessary, possible, and impossible things, and the non-finiteness of its relata, and the necessitation of its oneness. So the universality of its relation is due to its suitability for all. And the non-finiteness of its relata is due to the impossibility of specifying it with something finite; because that would be a preferment without a preferrer. And among its relata is the bliss of Paradise, which is not finite but is renewed little by little, and so on. And the necessitation of its oneness is because revelation did not indicate multiplicity; rather consensus has been reached on negating a second eternal speech, and similarity is only in the three mentioned judgments even if the aspect of relation differs. The Universal Attachment of Hearing, Sight, and Perception
Detailed commentary on lines affirming universal attachment of hearing, sight, and perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the divine attributes of hearing, sight, and perception are attached to every existent, yet each attribute has a distinct reality known only to Allah.

Core Idea
Unity of object does not mean unity of attributes.

In this passage from Tuhfat al-Murid, the commentator explains the theological claim that Allah's hearing, sight, and perception encompass all existents. The grammatical nuances help clarify that these attributes share the same object but remain distinct in their essential realities. This lesson will walk through the textual analysis and the theological implications, including the differing opinions on perception.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the grammatical explanations that clarify how the attachment is asserted.
Pay attention to the word 'فأنط' and the extra lam.
2
Identify the three attributes and their common object
The passage states that hearing, sight, and perception (if affirmed) are each attached to every existent. See how the commentator repeats 'كل موجود' for each.
3
Understand the key theological point: distinct attributes
The commentator explicitly says that the unity of the object does not imply unity of the attributes. Each attribute has a unique reality of unveiling.
This refutes a potential misunderstanding.
4
Examine the differing opinions on perception
The passage mentions two opinions: perception either encompasses all existents like hearing and sight, or is limited to tangible, smellable, and tastable things.
This shows scholarly divergence.
5
Reflect on the significance of following earlier scholars
The opening line 'فلنتبع' indicates the difficulty of this topic and the need to rely on transmitted knowledge from the people of insight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فَلْنَتَّبِعْ) بالنون أو بالتاء أوله، وفيه إشارة إلى غموض المحل وصعوبته، فيشير إلى أنه ليس لنا في هذا المقام إلا اتباع القوم، خصوصاً في إثبات التعلقات الأزليَّة. [٥. تعلقات السمع] ٣٦ - وَكُلُّ مَوْجُودٍ أَيْضًا لِلسَّمْعِ بِهْ كَذَا البَصَرْ إِدْرَاكُهُ إِنْ قِيلَ بِهْ قوله : (وَكُلُّ مَوْجُودٍ أَيْضًا لِلسَّمْعِ بِه) أي : وكل موجود علق للسمع به، فأنط : فعل به، أمر من الإناطة؛ وهي التعليق. وكلُّ : مبتدأ خبره جملة (أنط للسمع به)، أو مفعول لمحذوف يفسِّرُهُ المذكور من باب الاشتغال؛ على حد زيداً مرَّ به، والتقدير : اقصد كلَّ موجود، واللام في قوله: (للسمع) زائدةٌ، و(السمع) مفعول لـ (أنظ) بمعنى (علق)، أو ضمَّنَه معنى (اعترف) فعدَّاه باللام، وبالجملة فالمعنى: اعتقد تعلق السمع الأزلي بكل موجود. [٦. تعلقات البصر] وقوله : (كَذَا البَصَرُ)؛ أي: مثل السمع البصر في تعلقه بكل موجود، فاسم الإشارة راجع للسمع، و(كذا) خبر مقدم، و(البصر) مبتدأ مؤخَّر . [تعلقات الإرادة] وقوله : (إِدْرَاكُهُ) أي : وكذا إدراكه، فهو معطوف على البصر بحرف عطف مقدر . وقوله : (إِنْ قِيلَ بِه)؛ أي: إن قيل بثبوته، كما هو أحد الأقوال الثلاثة السابقة في قوله : فَهَلْ لَهُ إِدْرَاكَ أَو لا؟ خُلْفُ وَعِنْدَ قَوْمٍ صَحَ فِيهِ الوَقْفُ فهذه الصفاتُ الثلاثةُ متَّحدةُ المتعلَّقِ، ولا يلزم من اتحاد المتعلَّق اتحاد الصفة، بل الصفة متعددة، وكلٌّ منها له حقيقةً من الانكشاف ليست عين حقيقة غيره، لا يعلم تلك الحقيقة إلا الله تعالى. وما ذكره المصنف أن سمعه وبصره تعالى يتعلَّقان بكل موجود .. هو ما ذكره بعض المتأخرين؛ كالشيخ السنوسي ومن تبعه. والذي في كلام السعد وغيره أن السمع صفةٌ تتعلَّق بالمسموعات، وأنَّ البصر الأزليَّ صفةٌ تتعلق بالمبصرات، وهو محتمل للعموم والخصوص، فيحتمل أنه أراد المسموعات والمبصرات في تعالى وهي الموجودات فيكون موافقاً لما تقدَّم، ويحتمل أنه أراد المسموعات والمبصرات في حقنا؛ وهي الأصواتُ في الأول، والذوات والألوان في الثاني فيكون مخالفاً لما تقدم. وما ذكره المصنف أيضاً من كون الإدراك على القول به مثل السمع والبصر في التعلقِ بكل موجود هو أحد قولين قد سبق ذكرهما، وثانيهما : أنه يتعلَّقُ بالملموسات والمشمومات والمذوقات من غير اتصال بمحالها، فهما طريقتان للقوم كما يُؤخذ من «اليوسي، وشرح الكبرى.
His saying: (فَلْنَتَّبِعْ) – with a noon or a ta' at its beginning, and in it is an indication of the obscurity of the topic and its difficulty, so it indicates that we have nothing in this place except following the people (the scholars), especially in affirming the eternal relations. [5. Relations of Hearing] 36 – And every existent is also attached to hearing, likewise sight, its perception if it is affirmed. His saying: (وَكُلُّ مَوْجُودٍ أَيْضًا لِلسَّمْعِ بِه) meaning: and every existent is attached to hearing. فأنط: a verb used as a command, derived from الإناطة (attachment). And كل is either a subject whose predicate is the sentence (أنط للسمع به), or an object of an omitted verb that is explained by the mentioned one, from the باب الاشتغال, like 'Zaydan marra bihi', and the estimation is: intend every existent. And the lam in (للسمع) is extra, and (السمع) is the object of (أنظ) meaning 'attach', or it is given the meaning of (اعترف) so it is made transitive with the lam. In summary, the meaning is: believe in the eternal attachment of hearing to every existent. [6. Relations of Sight] And His saying: (كَذَا البَصَرُ) i.e., sight is like hearing in its attachment to every existent. So the demonstrative pronoun refers to hearing, and (كذا) is a preposed predicate, and (البصر) is a postponed subject. [Relations of Will] And His saying: (إِدْرَاكُهُ) i.e., and likewise its perception, so it is coordinated to 'sight' with an omitted coordinating conjunction. And His saying: (إِنْ قِيلَ بِه) i.e., if it is affirmed as existent, as it is one of the three previous opinions in his saying: 'So does He have perception or not? A dispute, and according to some people, suspension (waqf) is correct in it.' So these three attributes have a unified object (muttaḥid al-mutaʿallaq), and from the unity of the object it does not follow that the attributes are unified, rather the attributes are multiple, and each of them has a reality of unveiling (inkishaf) that is not the same as the reality of another. No one knows that reality except Allah the Exalted. And what the author mentioned, that His hearing and His sight are attached to every existent, is what some later scholars mentioned, like al-Shaykh al-Sanusi and those who followed him. And what is in the words of al-Saʿd and others is that hearing is an attribute related to audible things, and that eternal sight is an attribute related to visible things, and it is open to generality and particularity. So it is possible that he meant audible and visible things in relation to the Exalted, and they are existents, so it agrees with what preceded, and it is possible that he meant audible and visible things in relation to us, which are sounds in the first and essences and colors in the second, so it contradicts what preceded. And what the author also mentioned, that perception, if affirmed, is like hearing and sight in its attachment to every existent, is one of two opinions that have preceded. And the second opinion is that it relates to tangible, smellable, and tastable things without connection to their loci. So these are two methods of the scholars, as taken from al-Yusi and the commentary on al-Kubra.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line of poetry that asserts that hearing, sight, and perception are attached to every existent. The commentator begins by explaining the word 'فلنتبع', noting that it indicates the difficulty of the topic and that one must follow the earlier scholars (al-qawm), especially in affirming eternal relations. He then interprets the line: 'And every existent is also attached to hearing, likewise sight, its perception if it is affirmed.' He provides grammatical analysis, explaining that 'فأنط' is a command form derived from 'الإناطة' (attachment). He gives two possible analyses of 'كل' and explains that the lam in 'للسمع' is extra, with 'السمع' as object. The meaning is to believe in the eternal attachment of hearing to every existent. Then he explains that the same applies to sight, and for perception it is conditional on its affirmation, referencing the three earlier opinions on whether God has perception (idrak). He then notes that these three attributes have a unified object (every existent), but that does not imply unification of the attributes themselves; each attribute has a distinct reality of unveiling, known only to God. He then discusses differing opinions: some later scholars (like al-Sanusi) hold that hearing and sight relate to all existents, while others (like al-Saʿd al-Din al-Taftazani) say hearing relates to sounds and sight to visible things. The author's position (in the poem) is that hearing and sight are universal, which matches the first opinion. For perception, two opinions are given: one that it is universal like hearing and sight, and another that it relates to tangible, smellable, and tastable things. The commentator concludes that these represent two methods of the scholars.

Key Terms
تعلقات السمع
تعلقات البصر
تعلقات الإدراك
الإناطة
الاتحاد في المتعلق
اختلاف الصفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because hearing, sight, and perception all relate to every existent, they are actually one and the same attribute.
Correction: The commentator explicitly states that the unity of the object does not entail unity of the attributes; each attribute has a distinct reality of unveiling.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the second opinion on the object of perception (idrak)?
A) It relates to every existent like hearing and sight.
B) It relates only to sounds.
C) It relates to tangible, smellable, and tastable things without connection to their loci.
D) It has no object because perception is not real.

Key Takeaway
Hearing, sight, and perception each encompass all existents yet remain distinct attributes with unique realities known only to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that Allah’s hearing, sight, and perception all encompass every existent, yet remain distinct realities. When you sin in secret, which attribute do you most try to ignore—His hearing of your words, His sight of your actions, or His perception of your thoughts? What would it mean for you to live today as if each of these attributes is uniquely witnessing you?
?
The passage emphasizes that no one knows the true reality of these attributes except Allah. Does this humble you when you try to fully comprehend God? In what area of your life do you need to surrender your intellectual pride and simply worship Him as He has described Himself?
?
If perception is a distinct attribute, then Allah knows your innermost feelings and intentions in a way that is not merely hearing or seeing. When you think of a grudge you hold or a secret desire, are you comfortable that God perceives that exact reality? What would you need to change so that His perception of your heart brings you peace rather than unease?

Divine Attributes

Divine Hearing and Sight: Unity of Object, Multiplicity of Attributes
Explains the object of divine sight and its relation to hearing, with scholarly opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine hearing and sight share the same object (every existent) but are distinct attributes with unique realities of disclosure.

Core Idea
The unity of what God hears and sees does not make hearing and sight the same attribute.

This lesson unpacks a key principle in Islamic theology: although the attributes of hearing and sight both relate to every created thing, they are not identical. The commentator explains that each attribute has its own distinct reality of disclosure, known only to Allah. We will explore this principle and the two main scholarly interpretations of the objects of these attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on 'similarly the sight'
Read the first part of the Arabic passage explaining that the sight, like hearing, attaches to every existent. Notice how the demonstrative pronoun connects back to hearing.
The phrase 'كَذَا البَصَرُ' means 'similarly the sight'.
2
Understand the principle of unity of object
The commentator states that the three attributes (hearing, sight, perception) share a single object (all existents) but emphasizes that this does not make them one attribute. Each attribute has a unique 'reality of disclosure' (انكشاف).
This refutes any confusion that might arise from the shared object.
3
Compare the two scholarly views
Note that the author's view (from later scholars) is that hearing and sight attach to all existents. But the view of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani is that hearing attaches to sounds and sight to visible things. Consider the two interpretations of this view.
The difference hinges on whether 'audible' and 'visible' refer to their objects in relation to God (all existents) or to us (sounds and colors).
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters. It preserves the uniqueness of each attribute while acknowledging that God's knowledge encompasses all things without limitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (كَذَا البَصَرُ)؛ أي: مثل السمع البصر في تعلقه بكل موجود، فاسم الإشارة راجع للسمع، و(كذا) خبر مقدم، و(البصر) مبتدأ مؤخَّر . تعلقات الإرادة ] وقوله : (إِدْرَاكُهُ) أي : وكذا إدراكه، فهو معطوف على البصر بحرف عطف مقدر . وقوله : (إِنْ قِيلَ بِه)؛ أي: إن قيل بثبوته، كما هو أحد الأقوال الثلاثة السابقة في قوله : فَهَلْ لَهُ إِدْراكَ أَو لا؟ خُلْفُ وَعِنْدَ قَوْمٍ صَحَ فِيهِ الوَقْفُ فهذه الصفاتُ الثلاثةُ متَّحدةُ المتعلَّقِ، ولا يلزم من اتحاد المتعلَّق اتحاد الصفة، بل الصفة متعددة، وكلٌّ منها له حقيقةً من الانكشاف ليست عين حقيقة غيره، لا يعلم تلك الحقيقة إلا الله تعالى. وما ذكره المصنف أن سمعه وبصره من وبصره تعالى يتعلّقان بكل موجود .. هو ما ذكره بعض المتأخرين ؛ كالشيخ السنوسي ومن تبعه والذي في كلام السعد وغيره أن السمع صفةٌ تتعلَّق بالمسموعات، وأنَّ البصر الأزليَّ صفةٌ تتعلق بالمبصرات، وهو محتمل للعموم والخصوص، فيحتمل أنه أراد المسموعات والمبصرات في تعالى وهي الموجودات فيكون موافقاً لما تقدَّم، ويحتمل أنه أراد المسموعات والمبصرات في حقنا؛ وهي الأصواتُ في الأول، والذوات والألوان في الثاني فيكون مخالفاً لما تقدم. الأزلي حقه وما ذكره المصنف أيضاً من كون الإدراك على القول به مثل السمع والبصر في التعلقِ بكل موجود هو أحد قولين قد سبق ذكرهما، وثانيهما : أنه يتعلَّقُ بالملموسات والمشمومات والمذوقات من غير اتصال بمحالها، فهما طريقتان للقوم كما يُؤخذ من «اليوسي، وشرح الكبرى.
And His saying: (SIMILARLY THE SIGHT): i.e., like hearing, the sight in its attachment to every existent. So the demonstrative pronoun refers back to hearing, and (similarly) is a predicate in pre-position, and (the sight) is a subject in post-position. [Section on attachments of will] And His saying: (HIS PERCEPTION): i.e., and similarly His perception, for it is conjoined to 'the sight' by an implicit conjunction. And His saying: (IF IT IS SAID OF IT): i.e., if it is said with regard to its affirmation, as is one of the three previous opinions in his saying: 'So does He have perception or not? There is disagreement, and among some people the suspension of judgment is correct.' So these three attributes have a single object, and the unity of the object does not necessitate the unity of the attribute; rather, the attribute is multiple, and each of them has a reality of disclosure which is not the very reality of another; no one knows that reality except Allah Almighty. And what the author mentioned that His hearing and His sight — from His sight? — relate to every existent is what some later scholars mentioned, like Shaykh al-Sanusi and those who followed him. And what is in the speech of Sa'd and others is that hearing is an attribute that relates to audible things, and that eternal sight is an attribute that relates to visible things, and this is subject to generalization and specification. It is possible that he meant by audible and visible things in relation to Him, i.e., existents, and thus it would be in agreement with what preceded, and it is possible that he meant by audible and visible things in relation to us, i.e., sounds in the first, and essences and colors in the second, and thus it would be contrary to what preceded. The eternal [attribute] is correct? And what the author also mentioned regarding perception, on the opinion that it exists, being like hearing and sight in attaching to every existent, is one of two opinions that have been mentioned before. The second is that it attaches to tangible things, olfactory things, and gustatory things without contact with their loci. So these are two methods of the scholars, as taken from al-Yusi and Sharh al-Kubra.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the objects of divine hearing, sight, and perception. It begins by explaining the line of the poem: 'Similarly the sight' meaning that like hearing, sight attaches to every existent. Then it says that 'His perception' is similarly conjoined. It explains that the line 'If it is said of it' refers to the three opinions about perception. It then states that these three attributes (hearing, sight, perception) share a single object (every existent) but that does not mean they are identical; each has a distinct reality of disclosure. It then discusses two views: the author's view (that they attach to all existents) is from later scholars like al-Sanusi, while earlier scholars like Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani held that hearing attaches to sounds and sight to visible objects. Two interpretations are possible: either these are the objects in relation to God (i.e., all existents) or in relation to us (sounds and colors). It then mentions that for perception, there are two opinions: one that it attaches to all existents like hearing/sight, and another that it attaches to tangible, olfactory, and gustatory things without contact. This shows the range of scholarly disagreement.

بصر

انكشاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if hearing and sight both apply to all existents, they must be the same attribute.
Correction: The commentator explicitly states that unity of object does not necessitate unity of attribute; each has a distinct reality of disclosure.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of the three attributes having a single object?
A) They become one attribute.
B) They remain multiple attributes with distinct realities.
C) Their existence becomes doubtful.
D) They only apply to some existents.

Key Takeaway
Divine hearing and sight both encompass all existents, but they remain distinct attributes with unique inner realities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God hears every word you speak and sees every action you perform, would you change what you say and do today? What specific habit would you start or stop right now?
?
The scholars disagree on whether God's hearing is limited to sounds or extends to all existents. Which view makes you feel more accountable for your inner thoughts, and why? Commit to one concrete way you will live out that accountability before the next prayer.
?
God's hearing and sight are distinct attributes with unique realities beyond human comprehension. How does this truth affect the way you call upon Him in your du'a? Will you now address Him with a specific attribute (e.g., 'O All-Hearing, O All-Seeing') more intentionally? Choose one attribute to focus on in your next supplication and write down how that changes your mindset.

Divine Perception: Two Scholarly Opinions on Its Object
Explains the two opinions on the object of divine perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two competing opinions about the object of divine perception: whether it covers all existents like hearing and sight, or attaches to tangible, olfactory, and gustatory things.

Core Idea
Scholars debated whether divine perception extends to all things or only to sensed qualities.

This lesson focuses on the divine attribute of perception (إدراك). The commentator presents two opinions: one that perception, like hearing and sight, attaches to every existent, and another that it attaches specifically to tangible, olfactory, and gustatory things without contact with their loci. This disagreement reflects different theological approaches to defining God's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Locate the discussion on perception
Find the part of the passage that discusses 'إدراك' and the line 'إِنْ قِيلَ بِه'. This introduces the context that there are three opinions on whether God has perception.
2
Understand the first opinion
The first opinion, attributed to some scholars, is that perception attaches to every existent, just like hearing and sight.
This aligns with the principle of unity of object from the previous lesson.
3
Understand the second opinion
The second opinion is that perception attaches specifically to tangible, olfactory, and gustatory things. Note that it does not require contact with the 'loci' (i.e., the objects themselves).
This restricts perception to certain types of objects.
4
Compare the implications
Consider why scholars differed. The first opinion emphasizes God's comprehensive knowledge, while the second may be based on linguistic or scriptural considerations about what 'perception' typically means.

The Three Attachments of Hearing, Sight, and Perception
Enumerates the three attachments for hearing, sight, and perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of attachment (talluq) for the divine attributes of hearing, sight, and perception.

Core Idea
God's attributes have three modes of attachment: eternal actual, eternal potential, and contingent actual.

This lesson explores the intricate topic of how divine attributes relate to their objects. The author explains that hearing, sight, and perception each have three distinct attachments: one to God's essence, one to creation before existence, and one after existence. Understanding these helps clarify the nature of these attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage that enumerates the three attachments. Focus on the terms 'talluq tanjizi qadim', 'talluq suluhi qadim', and 'talluq tanjizi hadith'.
2
Identify the three categories
List the three categories with their definitions and examples as given in the passage.
Notice which attachment is eternal and which is contingent.
3
Understand the derivation
Notice how the imperative 'anẓur' implies the attachment and the generalizing particle implies unlimited objects.
This shows that the attributes are not limited to a specific type of relation.
4
Reflect on the silence
Why did the author remain silent about the unity of these attributes? The commentary explains it is known by analogy with power and will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنَّ للسمع والبصر والإدراك على القول به والقول بأنَّه يتعلق بكل موجود ثلاث تعلقات : تعلقاً تنجيزيا قديماً : وهو التعلق بذات الله وصفاته. وصلوحيًّا قديماً : وهو التعلق بنا قبل وجودنا . وتنجيزيا حادثاً : وهو التعلق بنا بعد وجودنا . التعلُّق لهذه الصفات مُستفاد من صيغة الأمر في قوله : (أنظ)، كما ووجوب استفيد عدم تناهي متعلقاتها من أداة العموم الداخلة على (موجود)، وسكت المصنف عن وحدة هذه الصفات للعلم بها من وجوبها لنظائرها ؛ كالقدرة والإرادة؛ إذ لا فرق. ولا إيطاء في كلام المصنف لاختلاف مرجع ،الضميرين، نظير ما تقدَّم في اسمي الإشارة في قوله : (ومثل ذي إرادة .. إلى آخره وسبق ما في نحوه ۳۷ - وَغَيْرُ عِلْمٍ هَذِهِ كَمَا نَبَتْ ثُمَّ الحَيَاةُ مَا بِشَيْ نَعَلَّقَتْ . قوله : (وَغَيْرُ عِلْمٍ هذِهِ أي : هذه الصفاتِ الأربع ـ وهي : الكلام، والسمع والبصر، والإدراك - غير العلم، فاسم الإشارة مبتدأ مؤخَّر، و (غير علم خبر مقدَّم، ودفع بذلك ما قد يتوهم من اتحادها مع العلم لاتحاد متعلق الكلام مع متعلّق العلم، واندراج متعلّق السمع والبصر والإدراك في متعلقه، لا سيما وتعلق هذه الثلاثة تعلق انكشاف كتعلَّقِ العلم، وكما أنَّ هذه الصفاتِ الأربع مغايرة للعلم بعضُها مغاير لبعض، واتحاد المتعلّق لا يوجب اتحاد الحقيقة. وقوله : كَمَا ثَبَتْ) أي: كالتغاير الذي ثبت عند القوم بالأدلة السمعيَّة؛ لأنَّ هذه الصفاتِ إِنَّما ثبتت بالسمع والمدلول لغةٌ لكلِّ واحدةٍ غيرُ المدلول للأُخرى، فوجب حمل ما ورد على ظاهره حتى يثبت خلافُهُ ، وبيان كون المدلول لغة لكلّ واحدة غير المدلول للأخرى، أنَّ السمعَ حِسُّ الأُذُنِ؛ أي حاستها، والأُذُنَ نفسها، وما وقر فيها من شيء تسمعه والذكر المسموع والبصرَ حِسُّ العين؛ أي حاستها، والكلام القولُ، وما كان مكتفياً بنفسه، والعلم : هو المعرفة كما يُؤخذ من «القاموس» في مواضع متعددة، وإذا ثبت أنها متغايرة لغةً كانت متغايرةً شرعاً، وبالجملة: فكنه كل واحدة غير كنه الأخرى، ونفوض علم ذلك الله تعالى.
Know that for hearing, sight, and perception, on the opinion that it exists and the opinion that it relates to every existent, there are three attachments: an eternal actual attachment: which is the attachment to the essence of Allah and His attributes; an eternal potential attachment: which is the attachment to us before our existence; and a contingent actual attachment: which is the attachment to us after our existence. The attachment for these attributes is derived from the imperative form in His saying (anẓur), just as the obligation and the non-limitation of their objects is derived from the generalizing particle that enters upon (mawjūd). The author remains silent about the unity of these attributes because it is known from their necessity to their counterparts, like power and will; for there is no difference. And there is no redundancy in the author's speech due to the difference of the referent of the two pronouns, analogous to what was said earlier regarding the two demonstrative pronouns in his saying (wa mithl dhī irāda ... etc.). And what preceded regarding its like. 37 - AND OTHER THAN KNOWLEDGE, THESE AS IT IS ESTABLISHED? THEN LIFE, IT IS NOT ATTACHED TO ANYTHING. His saying: (AND OTHER THAN KNOWLEDGE, THESE) i.e., these four attributes — which are speech, hearing, sight, and perception — are other than knowledge. So the demonstrative pronoun is a delayed subject, and (other than knowledge) is an advanced predicate. By this he repels what might be imagined of their unity with knowledge due to the unity of the object of speech with the object of knowledge, and the inclusion of the objects of hearing, sight, and perception in its object, especially since the attachment of these three is a disclosure attachment like the attachment of knowledge. And just as these four attributes are distinct from knowledge, some of them are distinct from others; and the unity of the object does not necessitate the unity of the essence. And his saying: (AS IT IS ESTABLISHED) i.e., like the distinctness that is established among the people by scriptural proofs; because these attributes are only established by scripture, and the linguistic denotation of each one is other than the linguistic denotation of the other. So it is necessary to take what is reported in its literal sense until its contrary is established. The explanation that the linguistic denotation of each is other than the linguistic denotation of the other: that hearing is the sense of the ear, i.e., its faculty, and the ear itself, and what is placed in it of something one hears, and the memory of what is heard; and sight is the sense of the eye, i.e., its faculty; and speech is the saying, and what is self-sufficient; and knowledge is cognition, as taken from al-Qamus in multiple places. And if it is established that they are linguistically distinct, then they are theologically distinct. In summary, the essence of each one is other than the essence of the other, and we consign the knowledge of that to Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage does two things. First, it enumerates the three types of attachment (talluq) for the divine attributes of hearing, sight, and perception (on the opinion that they attach to all existents): eternal actual (to God's essence and attributes), eternal potential (to us before we exist), and contingent actual (to us after we exist). It notes that the imperative form 'anẓur' (look/consider) implies these attachments, and the generalizing particle implies their objects are unlimited. Then the commentator explains that the author omitted discussion of the unity of these attributes because it is known by analogy with power and will. Second, the passage comments on the line 'Other than knowledge, these as it is established' and launches into an argument that these four attributes (speech, hearing, sight, perception) are distinct from knowledge and from each other. The potential confusion arises because they share the same object (all existents) and have a similar 'disclosure' nature. The commentator refutes this by invoking linguistic distinctions: in language, each term refers to a different sense or concept (e.g., hearing is ear-sense, sight is eye-sense, speech is utterance, knowledge is cognition). Since scripture establishes these attributes, we must take them in their literal sense, and thus they are distinct theologically. The passage concludes that the true essence of each is known only to Allah.

تعلق صلوحي
قديم

According to the passage, what is the eternal potential attachment?
A) to God's essence
B) to us before existence
C) to us after existence
D) to all existents

Key Takeaway
The three attachments of hearing, sight, and perception show that divine attributes relate to their objects in different modes: eternal actual, eternal potential, and contingent actual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that God's hearing and sight have an eternal potential attachment to you before you were born. Does this knowledge change how you view your own existence and purpose? Will you live today as if you are already fully known and heard by God, even in your innermost thoughts?
?
The passage derives God's attachment to creation from the imperative 'anẓur' (look/consider). If God commands you to look, are you truly looking at His signs with the intention to see His attributes? What is one specific sign of God you have overlooked today that you now commit to reflecting on?
?
God's actual attachment to you after your existence is contingent—it depends on your existence. Yet His potential attachment was eternal. How does this difference affect your sense of accountability? Are you living as if God's hearing and sight are currently attached to you in every moment, or do you sometimes forget that He sees and hears all?

Divine Attributes

Distinguishing Divine Attributes from Knowledge
Argues that four attributes are distinct from knowledge using linguistic distinctions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that the divine attributes of speech, hearing, sight, and perception are distinct from knowledge and from each other, based on linguistic evidence.

Core Idea
These four attributes are distinct from knowledge because their linguistic meanings differ, even though they share the same object.

The previous lesson established the attachments of hearing, sight, and perception. Now we turn to a common confusion: are these attributes actually the same as knowledge? The commentator argues they are not, using linguistic definitions and scriptural proofs. This lesson dives into that argument and why the unity of the object does not imply unity of essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the commentary on the line 'Other than knowledge, these as it is established'. Note the potential confusion addressed.
2
Understand the confusion
The confusion arises because all these attributes have the same object (all existents) and involve disclosure (inkishaf).
3
Examine the linguistic evidence
Look at the definitions: hearing (sense of ear), sight (sense of eye), speech (saying), knowledge (cognition). Note how each is distinct in language.
The commentator uses al-Qamus as reference.
4
Conclude the argument
Because they are linguistically distinct, they are theologically distinct. The true essence is known only to Allah.
